Commentary

The Origin of the Anglo-French Rapprochement 26

— Heng

Great Britain's policy towards continental Europe has always been impartial between Germany and France. However, since last year, its attitude has gradually changed. Initially, it tacitly approved of the Franco-Russian alliance. Then, it supported Soviet Russia's entry into the League of Nations. This year, it not only expressed sympathy for the Franco-Italian agreement, but also coordinated with France on February 3. At the Stresa Conference, it formed a united front with France and Italy against Germany. Furthermore, in the League of Nations Council, it supported France in condemning Germany's abrogation of treaties. Looking at its actions as a whole, before a situation is determined, it often remains silent, appearing to sympathize with Germany. But in the end, it invariably opposes Germany. It seems that today, the British people harbor some suspicion and concern toward Germany. Its relatively detached attitude toward European disputes is probably still aimed at acting as a mediator.

What, then, are the reasons for Britain's current distrust of Germany? According to our observations, one reason is the impetus given by the German authorities' vigorous and unprecedented actions. Hitler and the National Socialists are determined to restore Germany to its pre-war status, advancing bravely and disregarding everything. Last year's actions in the Saarland already showed a "burn the bridges" attitude. If its strength were sufficient, it would not hesitate to provoke war. However, today's Britain, focused on maintaining its prosperity and security, cannot, based on past sympathy, plunge into a vortex that threatens its own safety. This is why it supports the French plan, taking the pacification of the European situation as its mission.

Secondly, it is due to the rapid development of the German air force. Last spring, Göring declared that Germany needed 1,200 aircraft. Later, a semi-official German newspaper argued that Germany should have 6,000 aircraft. Recently, Hitler even demanded equality in air power from Britain. Outsiders cannot know how many military aircraft Germany actually has today. However, judging from the implications of its demands on Britain, it is clear that a very large air force already exists in reality, or at least gives that impression. During the last World War, the German air force used Belgium as a base to repeatedly attack Britain, posing a major threat to Britain. In the eighteen years since then, the progress of air power far exceeds that of the past. Therefore, even if Germany has no base in Belgium, and if there is discord between Britain and Germany, the German air force could still threaten Britain. It takes only two hours to reach London from the Rhineland region of Germany, and three hours to reach Wales. Therefore, today, if Britain wants to defend against German air raids, its first line of defense cannot be on its own coast, but must be pushed to the borders of countries like the Netherlands and Belgium. This is what Baldwin meant when he said that Britain's defense was no longer on the Dover coast, but on the Rhine. Defending against air raids requires ample time for deployment, such as the take-off of defense aircraft, the arrangement of formations, the concealment of urban targets, and informing the public, all of which must be done in advance. According to calculations by military experts, the first line of defense against air raids must be at least 150 miles outside the national border, otherwise it will be difficult to cope. Therefore, today, northern France and the Netherlands and Belgium are the most suitable defense lines for Britain against German air raids. The reason why Britain today values the safety of the Netherlands and Belgium and maintains wartime friendship with France lies in this. This is also the reason why it initiated the "Air Pact." In the past, the Locarno Treaty only obligated Britain to assist France, but the "Air Pact" stipulates that not only must Britain assist France, but if Britain is in trouble, France must also assist Britain. The relationship of mutual support and defense is naturally extremely close. Understanding this, it is not difficult to understand the increasingly close relationship between Britain and France over the past year.

Hitler Convenes Party, Government, and Military Conference in Munich to Discuss Formal Reply to the League of Nations; Document Finalized and Issued Yesterday 27

(Berlin) It is announced here that Germany's formal reply to the League of Nations' condemnation of its rearmament plan will be issued on Saturday. The government strongly opposes the League of Nations' resolution. Führer Hitler has convened a special meeting of senior National Socialist authorities in Munich to draft the reply. Those attending also include Foreign Minister Neurath and military experts Ribbentrop, etc. Army Minister Blomberg is also present. As for whether the form of the reply will be a declaration by the Führer or a statement with the government seal, this is not yet known here. However, observers predict that Germany's world policy will likely undergo an astonishing development. Officials say that, in any case, Germany will solemnly declare that the League of Nations' condemnation has made it impossible for Germany to rejoin this international body. Furthermore, British Ambassador to Germany, Phipps, yesterday, on behalf of Britain and Italy, re-warned Germany not to further damage the demilitarized zone of the Rhineland. The German government has not yet announced its attitude on this matter. (19th National Telegram)

(London) The entire European diplomatic community is very anxious today. According to news from Munich, Germany, Führer Hitler is preparing to launch another "bomb" on international diplomacy. At the same time, France and Russia's plan to encircle Germany with military force is also intensifying. However, most countries want to wait quietly for Germany's reply to the League of Nations' condemnation before taking action. According to news here, Germany has expressed its opposition to the League of Nations' resolution to Britain and France. Its formal reply is already being prepared. The general opinion in Britain is that Hitler will adopt a calm attitude and is unlikely to carry out his threat of non-cooperation with the various international agreements under consideration. The Associated Press has learned that when British Ambassador to Germany, Phipps, visited the German Foreign Office, German Foreign Minister Representative, Bülow, explained Germany's views on the League of Nations' resolution. Phipps also formally notified the German Foreign Office that Britain and Italy, in the Stresa Declaration, had reiterated their responsibility for the Locarno Treaty. Officials say that efforts are currently being made to ensure that Germany participates in cooperation on a friendly basis in various non-aggression plans to maintain peace in Eastern Europe. However, if Germany refuses to participate, an effective front can also be formed, at least temporarily preventing bloodshed. Foreign Secretary Simon is confident that Britain's peace plan will not fail, and the British people have given him full authority to handle it. (19th National Telegram)

Germany Lodges Verbal Protest; Britain Ignores It; Cabinet Members Leave for Easter Vacation 28

(Berlin) British Ambassador to Germany, Sir Phipps, was invited to the German Foreign Ministry today, where General Bülow, representing Foreign Minister Neurath, lodged a verbal protest in strong terms against Britain's attitude at the Stresa Conference and the League of Nations Council meeting. The Italian ambassador was also present. It is believed that Bülow asked the two ambassadors whether Britain and Italy, as guarantors of the Locarno Treaty, would consider themselves able to fulfill their responsibilities in the event of a future French invasion to the same extent as their responsibilities towards a German invasion. It is said that both ambassadors replied in the affirmative. Britain has ignored the German protest. According to news from London, cabinet members are now finalizing their official duties in order to take a break for Easter. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Litvinov Goes to Paris to Sign Franco-Soviet Pact; One Point Remains to Be Negotiated 29

(Paris) Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov has departed from Geneva and is scheduled to arrive here tomorrow to continue negotiations with French authorities on the Mutual Assistance Pact. Foreign Minister Laval was originally scheduled to visit Russia on the 23rd of this month, but due to Litvinov's visit to France, the trip has been postponed until early next month after the elections of the municipal councilors of various cities. Currently, the two governments have reached an agreement on the basic clauses of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. The pact stipulates that if one of the contracting states, not provoking other countries, is invaded by another country, the other contracting state shall immediately provide assistance. In order to prevent this obligation from conflicting with the obligations of the Locarno Pact, France has proposed a method to which the Soviet Union has not yet expressed agreement, so further negotiations are necessary. According to the Locarno Pact, France and Germany agree to respect the Rhine border, but if one of the two countries engages in aggression, and the League of Nations Council recognizes it as such, the other contracting states may not be bound by this clause. (18th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov departed from Geneva today for Paris. As for the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty, Foreign Ministry officials are now, together with Soviet Ambassador to France, Potemkin, organizing the wording of the articles. If Moscow and Paris reach a final agreement, the treaty will be initialed tomorrow by Foreign Minister Laval and Litvinov, and Franco-Soviet relations will henceforth move a step further. Furthermore, Laval was originally scheduled to go to Moscow around April 20th, but because Litvinov has already come to Paris, Laval will postpone the trip to Russia until May. (19th Havas Telegram)

(Paris) All newspapers are closely watching the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact, believing that the organizational work is quite complicated, and the formal signing may be delayed for a few days, but there do not seem to be any major difficulties. Le Petit Journal said, "The final articles of this treaty may be initialed on Saturday or Sunday." Le Journal said, "The content of the Franco-Soviet pact is different from the original form of the Eastern European Mutual Assistance Pact. The Soviet Union has concerns about its national security, and the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact should console it. However, Poland should not be put in a difficult position, either reluctantly approving it or becoming an enemy of France and the Soviet Union. The Soviet Union may not feel unhappy about this, because the Franco-Polish alliance has not died out." L'Économiste said, "Foreign Minister Laval's visit to Warsaw will not be fruitless. The Franco-Polish military alliance has not died out. It would not be a miscalculation if Poland made Germany aware of this in its relations with Germany." (19th Havas Telegram)

Czech Foreign Minister to Go to Moscow to Sign Soviet-Czech Agreement; Negotiations Proceed Smoothly 30

(Paris) European politicians are now engaged in negotiating new agreements, aiming to prevent the possibility of future wars. It is learned here today that Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov and Czech Foreign Minister Beneš held discussions before public lawyers, aiming to conclude a mutual assistance agreement. Everything will be modeled after the Franco-Soviet agreement recently negotiated, which is intended to replace the Eastern European Pact in the event that Germany and Poland refuse to participate in the Eastern European Pact. It is heard that the Soviet-Czech negotiations are proceeding very smoothly, and Czech Foreign Minister Beneš will probably go to Moscow within days to sign the first word of the new agreement. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Germany's Recruitment Regulations; April 21st Designated as Air Force Day 31

(Berlin) The government has recently issued formal regulations for the recruitment of new soldiers into the national defense forces, stipulating that only young men who are physically strong and without defects may join the national defense forces. However, if they are decisive, mentally strong, full of righteousness, and have been physically trained in their youth, then even if they have physical defects, they may still be allowed to enlist if necessary. All new soldiers must be at least one meter and fifty-four centimeters tall. Before enlisting, they must first undergo a physical examination by a doctor, divided into six grades: (1) qualified, (2) eligible, but with conditions, (3) temporarily ineligible, (4) qualified with restrictions, (5) unqualified, (6) absolutely unqualified. (18th Havas News Agency Telegram)

(Berlin) Germany's recruitment of new soldiers will be limited to qualified candidates, especially focusing on physical fitness. It is planned that the official regulations will be announced today, stipulating that the results of the doctor's physical examination will only be notified to the person being examined or their relatives. The aim is to recruit only strong and healthy new soldiers. Their height must reach one hundred and fifty-four centimeters, while volunteers must be one hundred and sixty centimeters tall. Air Force personnel must be between one hundred and sixty-five and one hundred and ninety centimeters tall. New recruits for the Air Force must not have color blindness or deafness. (19th National Telegram)

(Berlin) The Ministry of Defense has ordered that April 21st be designated as "Air Force Day." April 21st is the day of the death of Baron von Richthofen, the famous German pilot during the European War. Therefore, the Ministry of Aviation has designated this day every year as Air Force Day in his memory. This year's Air Force Day falls on a Sunday and also coincides with the Easter holiday, so there will be a grand celebration. German pilots will march through the streets of Berlin on this day. (18th Havas News Agency Telegram)

Poland Evaluates League of Nations Resolution as a Mere Formality; Negotiations Still Necessary in the End 32

Warsaw The semi-official Polish Guide Newspaper editorial criticized the Geneva resolution, stating that the passage of the resolution by the three Western European countries is only a formality, without a practical course of action. What was passed is only a principle, not a practical step. Therefore, the task today is still to bring this issue to an end without creating a deeper level of dispute. Polish Foreign Minister Beck has systematically addressed the unclear points, saying that creating an environment in Eastern Europe that fully benefits Poland, thereby promoting universal peace, is an urgent task. The newspaper's Berlin telegram also said that the Geneva resolution is certainly not welcome to Germany, but Hitler should be able to distinguish between form and reality. In terms of reality, Germany's unilateral abrogation of treaties and the restoration of conscription have not been sanctioned. Furthermore, Foreign Secretary Simon has solemnly declared that the door to future negotiations is still fully open. Germany should not be excluded from this. Therefore, the Geneva resolution may cause resentment in Germany, but it should not lead it astray. (19th National Telegram)

Anglo-German Naval Negotiations; German Counselor Returns Home to Report 33

(London) The naval counselor of the German Embassy in Britain has recently departed for home. According to naval sources in London, the counselor's return home is to report to the government on Britain's views on Germany's increase in naval tonnage. Naval sources also said that although naval experts from Britain and Germany are currently holding talks, it should not be assumed that Britain has already accepted Germany's naval demands. This discussion should only be based on the provisions of existing treaties; Britain does not want to hear anything else. (18th Havas Telegram)

Borah Opposes League of Nations Condemning Germany; Recommends Senate Ban Loans to Europe 34

(Washington) Progressive Republican Senator Borah today spared no sarcasm in criticizing the League of Nations' resolution condemning Germany. Borah today submitted a bill to the Senate to ban loans to any country outside the American continent, fearing that the United States would "again be drawn into the whirlpool of disputes by these powerful forces." Borah then said, "The fact that the League of Nations is controlled by a few powerful European countries for the sake of peace is the most concrete evidence of this." (19th National News Agency Telegram)

US Arms Investigation; Senate Committee Cautious to Avoid International Disputes 35

(Washington) Last year, the Senate Arms Investigation Committee discovered several facts in the ledgers of Morgan & Co. and the letters of the company's representative in Britain during the European War, which were related to the United States' declaration of war against Germany in 1917, and attached great importance to them. However, the committee's investigation often involved foreign countries and had caused opposition from foreign countries. Therefore, the matter of Morgan & Co. was discussed with President Roosevelt, and it was decided afterward that "in future investigations, any involvement of other countries that could cause disputes should be avoided." (18th Havas Telegram)

Leader of Austrian Defense Force Convicted of Conspiracy; 21 Defendants Belong to the Socialist Party; Sentences Range from 18 to 2 Years 36

(Vienna) The military court today found 21 leaders of the Socialist Party Defense Force guilty of conspiracy. Major Eifler was sentenced to 18 years in prison, Captain Rudolf was sentenced to 15 years in prison, and the remaining 19 were sentenced to terms ranging from 10 to 2 years. All claimed to be innocent. It is said that they had secretly met in a Socialist newspaper office to plot a rebellion. A large police force was stationed in the court to protect it during today's trial, but no demonstrations occurred. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Mass Arrests of Politicians Lead to Resignation of Bulgarian Cabinet; Purely Military Government to Be Formed 37

Sofia The arrest of many opposition leaders on political charges and their confinement in Burgas, Eastern Rumelia, has triggered a serious political crisis in Bulgaria. The cabinet has submitted its resignation today, protesting the mass arrests of politicians. The situation in Sofia, Bulgaria, is extremely tense, as the leaders of the Bulgarian Socialist Party, former Prime Minister Tsankov and General Georgiev, have been arrested, causing widespread fear. Troops are stationed in camps all day, preparing to deal with events. Tsankov was arrested for distributing leaflets to his comrades, defying the law abolishing political parties. Former Police Chief Nachemov is also among those arrested. It is expected that a military cabinet will be formed. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Sofia General Slavev, the Prime Minister, reported to reporters that the resignation of the Bulgarian cabinet was approved by the King this afternoon. At the same time, the King ordered the current Prime Minister to temporarily maintain the status quo pending the formation of a new cabinet. Slavev later said that he took this action because former Prime Minister Georgiev and several of his political allies had been constantly conspiring to overthrow the government. In addition, Professor Zankov also frequently attacked the government, demanding the return of the troops to their camps, so that the unity of the royal family, the army, and the state could be restored. Recently, another conspiracy was discovered, so Slavev ordered the arrest and expulsion of Georgiev and Zankov. However, this action of his prompted those in the cabinet who sympathized with him to leave. How to deal with this matter in the future will be according to the King's wishes, but the King's intentions have not yet been expressed. (18th National News Agency Telegram)

German Religious Dispute; National Socialist Party Does Not Intend to Interfere; Six More Pastors Arrested 38

(Berlin) The National Socialist Party will remain on the sidelines of the German religious dispute. After party leaders met in Munich, they failed to formulate any intervention plan. The arrest of pastors in Saxony is continuing. Yesterday, 200 pastors there petitioned the authorities to release the detained pastors, otherwise they would ask that the petitioners be arrested and imprisoned together. But the authorities arrested six more people, shaved their heads, and sent them to concentration camps. (18th Reuters Telegram)

Greece to Amend Constitution; Increase Government Power; Accomplices Separately Sentenced 39

Athens Greece will now implement constitutional amendments to increase the power of the government. Today, the State Council sent a resolution to the Constitutional Committee, outlining the general principles to be included in the new constitution, namely: (1) The Chamber of Deputies shall exercise legislative power; the Chamber of Deputies may organize other deliberative bodies separately, but their task shall be limited to consultation only. (2) Only the government has the right to propose laws regarding national expenditures. (4) The President of the Republic has the power to dissolve the Chamber of Deputies, subject to prior proposal by the Cabinet. (5) The President shall be elected by direct vote of the citizens. In addition, the resolution further advocates that the power of the legislative body to vote on the issue of confidence in the government should be limited, that there should be absolute freedom of assembly and association, but that the legislative body has the right to temporarily restrict it when necessary, and that the same applies to freedom of speech. Furthermore, the clause in the Constitution prohibiting the Greek people from wearing medals should be abolished. (18th Havas Telegram)

Thessaloniki, Greece After the failure of former Greek Prime Minister Venizelos' rebellion, the accomplices everywhere were tried by military courts. The Thessaloniki Garrison Military Court tried 52 rebels, and the verdicts were announced last night. Two defendants were sentenced to life imprisonment, five were sentenced to prison for terms ranging from 6 to 15 years, 18 were sentenced to prison for terms of 5 years or less, and 27 were acquitted. Furthermore, the Larissa District Court is scheduled to begin hearing the case of members of parliament, journalists, and civilians belonging to the Venizelos party today. There are a total of 60 defendants, no fewer than 250 witnesses, and more than 30 defense lawyers. It is estimated that this case will last for six days. In addition, the accomplices among the resident officers in Thessaloniki and Kilkis districts will be brought to trial by the military court tomorrow. (19th Havas Telegram)

Japanese Representatives Depart for Europe to Attend International Labor Conference 40

League of Nations Agrees to Send Commissioner to Assist with Yunnan-Burma Boundary Demarcation 41

(Geneva) The Yunnan Province and Burma border's southern section boundary demarcation matters have been settled by China and Britain to organize a boundary demarcation committee. China and Britain will each send two commissioners, and the chairman of the League of Nations Council will appoint a neutral country commissioner to serve as chairman. (18th Havas Telegram)

Dumping of Japanese Goods Harms US Industry; US Congressmen Loudly Appeal to Congress 42

(Washington) Congressman Rogers stated to the House today the circumstances of Japanese goods affecting US industry, saying that New England suffered the most due to Japanese goods competition. Congress was very surprised by this. Rogers asked and answered himself, saying, "How can Japan eliminate US industry?" The answer is that goods that Americans cannot sell for less than three and a half dollars can be purchased in Japan for one dollar and two and a half cents. US flashlight manufacturers must receive fifty-nine cents to meet costs, while Japanese manufacturers only need thirty-nine cents. Rogers further said that some American fabrics cost one dollar and seventy-seven cents to manufacture, while Japanese manufacturers only need fifty-eight cents, and there is still profit to be made. (18th National Telegram)

Solar Eclipse Visible in Hokkaido, Japan in June Next Year 43

(Tokyo) A solar eclipse will be visible in Hokkaido, Japan on June 19th next year. The Japanese astronomical observatory is preparing to observe it and will soon send invitations to various countries to invite them to participate in the observation. Professor Mitchell of the University of Virginia in the United States recently wrote to Dr. Saotome, Director of the Astronomical Observatory, stating that dozens of American scholars will come to Japan on a naval special service ship to observe. It is heard that Professor Stratton, Director of the Solar Physics Observatory at Cambridge University in Britain, and six scholars will also come to Japan on a special ship. It is reported that China also has a plan to observe the solar eclipse. The Academia Sinica, with an expenditure of 150,000 yuan, organized a Chinese Solar Eclipse Observation Committee. Yu Qing-song, Director of the Nanjing Astronomical Observatory, and his scholars will participate in the observation in Boli, Russia. (19th Japanese Allied Telegram)

False Organization's Monopoly on Kerosene, Violating the Open Door Policy: Britain and the United States Lodge Another Protest with Japan 44

(Washington) The State Department announced today that the United States has once again protested to Japan against the "Manchukuo's" monopoly on kerosene. The government solemnly stated that the reason for the repeated protests is that this monopoly has a greater impact than the American oil industry in the Far East. It is understood that the United States believes that this move concerns a very important principle, which may have a profound impact on the relations between countries in the Pacific. If "Manchukuo" is allowed to establish a kerosene monopoly, then monopolies on other commodities can also be established in the future. If this continues, Manchuria will eventually have no free trade. Deputy Secretary of State Phillips stated this afternoon that Ambassador Grew in Japan has been instructed to reiterate the U.S. position to Japan. The United States believes that "Manchukuo's" monopoly on kerosene violates the Open Door Policy, and Japan cannot evade responsibility for "Manchukuo's" actions. The U.S. Ambassador was also instructed to review previous U.S. declarations, namely that the United States reserves all rights under international treaties regarding Manchuria. It is reported that the previous protests lodged with Japan by Britain, the United States, and the Netherlands have not received satisfactory replies. Japan only stated that it is not responsible for the actions of "Manchukuo." (National News Agency dispatch of the 18th)

(Tokyo) The British and American governments have protested to the Japanese government regarding the implementation of the petroleum monopoly law by "Manchukuo," stating that it violates the Open Door Policy. The Japanese government replied to the British government on March 25th, and then replied to the U.S. government on April 10th with a document containing largely the same content. However, on the 11th of this month, the British side instructed its ambassador to Japan, Sir Clive, and the American side instructed its ambassador to Japan, Grew, on the 15th of this month to meet with Foreign Minister Hirota, respectively. After expressing the intention of their respective governments to not recognize the third memorandum from Japan, they also submitted formal documents to draw attention and at the same time inquire about the true intentions of the Japanese government. Foreign Minister Hirota stated that the Japanese government had already clearly expressed its true intentions in the response memorandum and believed that there was no need for any changes. However, if British and American oil merchants wish to substantively negotiate with "Manchukuo," Japan would not hesitate to act as an intermediary. Therefore, the position of the Japanese government was solemnly clarified orally, and Japan's position was explained. (Nippon Rengo dispatch of the 19th)

Manchurian Soybeans and Rice Exported to Britain: Britain Decides to Increase Tax Rates in Response to Requests from the West Indies and Ceylon 45

(London) Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain has decided to stipulate new tax rates for grains, rice, and soybeans in the next budget, increasing import tariffs on grains, rice, and soybeans imported from Manchuria. It is reported that this measure is based on the recommendations of the Liverpool Chamber of Commerce and in response to requests from the British West Indies and Ceylon. Since the increase in imports of grains, rice, and soybeans produced in Manchuria, the import of similar goods from the West Indies and Ceylon to the United Kingdom has greatly decreased. Therefore, the West Indies and Ceylon specifically requested the British government to provide assistance in order to develop the colonies' exports to the United Kingdom. At the same time, it is permitted to restrict the import quota of Japanese cotton cloth in the two colonies, so as to increase the import of British goods. (Havas dispatch of the 18th)

Large-Scale U.S. Naval Maneuvers in the North Pacific: Japan Feels Threatened 46

(Tokyo) Despite strong opposition from the American people, the U.S. Navy is determined to be active in the North Pacific and conduct large-scale naval exercises in the area. This is a free action of the U.S. Navy. Although the Japanese Navy absolutely avoids criticism, it attaches great importance to this matter from the following perspectives: The northern end of the U.S. Navy's exercise area, Attu Island, is only 700 nautical miles from the northern end of the Japanese Kuril Islands and only 1,700 nautical miles from the base of the Northern Army in Tatzihaba. Starting exercises so close to Japanese territory and bases is no different from Japan establishing a base in the Marshall Islands and starting exercises. If Japan were to conduct exercises in this way, it is questionable whether the United States would be stimulated. Therefore, the U.S. Navy's exercise this time may not make the Japanese Navy nervous, and it cannot but doubt the true intention of the U.S. Navy. (Den Tsushin dispatch of the 19th)

Russia Establishes New Air Route in the North Pacific, Which Can Connect with U.S. Alaska: Japan Believes It Contains Military Significance 47

(Tokyo) According to a report received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from the Consul General in Khabarovsk, the Soviet Union has started the operation of the Far East air route from Moscow to the Shmidta Peninsula on the coast of the North Pacific. The Ministry of Military Affairs believes that this air route has a major relationship with Japan's national defense and attaches great importance to its future. (Nippon Rengo dispatch of the 19th)

(Tokyo) According to a report received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs from the Japanese Consulate in Khabarovsk, the Soviet Union has extended its postal air route between Moscow and Khabarovsk to Nikolayevsk-on-Amur and newly opened an air route from Nikolayevsk-on-Amur to the Shmidta Peninsula, encircling the North Pacific. In addition, according to the Ministry of Communications, this air route has a lot of military significance. The Shmidta Peninsula is very close to U.S. Alaska. There is already an air route between New York and Alaska, so the Soviet Union's new air route can connect with Alaska and New York. (Hua Lian dispatch of the 19th)

Japan Expresses Views on U.S.-Asia Aviation 48

(Tokyo) Pan American Airways' plan to fly across the Pacific Ocean to connect U.S. and Asian aviation has now achieved success in the first step of connecting San Francisco and Hawaii. In terms of the U.S. Far East aviation policy, it can be said to have established a major foundation, arousing attention from all sides. Wake Island is a restricted defense area stipulated by the Washington Naval Treaty, and the airfield established by Pan American Airways is located there. Since Wake Island is U.S. territory and the airfield is for commercial aircraft, it should not have any military significance. If according to the U.S. side's opinion, Japan has no need to criticize it. However, the company planning U.S.-Asia connection has not mentioned anything about Japan-U.S. aviation connection in advance. Given the current state of Japan-U.S. transportation, this fact has to be considered an unexpected situation. The section of the air route from San Francisco to Manila is close to the Sea of Japan and flies across Japan's South Seas Mandate Territory. It is extremely unpleasant that it is being constructed without any contact with Japan. Therefore, from the perspective of Japan-U.S. relations centered on Pacific transportation, it is necessary to express regret. (Nippon Rengo dispatch of the 19th)

U.S. House Committee Rejects Amendment to Banking Bill 49

(Washington) The House Banking and Currency Committee today rejected an amendment to the banking bill. According to this amendment, the Federal Reserve Board should try to stabilize current prices according to the prices of 1926. Now that this amendment has been rejected, it is expected that the review of this bill can be completed quickly. At that time, the Banking Committee will report to the House, advocating that it be passed in its original form. From then on, the Federal Reserve Board's power to control reserve banks will be further expanded. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

(Washington) The House of Representatives today overwhelmingly rejected Townsend's proposed old-age pension plan. According to this plan, anyone over the age of sixty would receive a pension of $200 per month. This money would be raised by levying a 2% tax on any business. People consider this plan purely ideal and not feasible. The authorities also opposed it, so the plan was eventually rejected. (Reuters dispatch of the 18th)

The land prices in various districts of Nanchang County have been estimated. The highest price for irrigated land is 41 yuan per mu, and the lowest is 25 yuan. Northwest Inspection Notes 88

— By our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

Changwu County, a Vital Point in Gansu and Shaanxi

Seventeen kilometers east of Pingliang is a town called Sishilipu, with a large population. Several dozen small carts come and go. Thirteen kilometers further is Baishui, also with a considerable population. There is a newly built old-style theater stage, with elaborate oil paintings. Another ten kilometers leads to Wangcun. Along the southern foothills, a new road is being built, but it is not yet completed. The Jing River meanders like a ring and must be crossed by wading. Fifteen kilometers away is Jingchuan, where the Rui River flows south to join the Jing. A mountain juts out at the confluence of the Jing and Rui, about thirty meters high, forming a triangle. A solitary tree grows at the top, and two or three temples are built in the middle. One is a three-story building called the Western Queen Mother Temple. At the foot of the mountain is a stone tablet inscribed "Ancient Yaochi, where the Queen Mother descended." Legend has it that King Mu of Zhou drove his eight steeds to meet the Western Queen Mother at Yaochi, which is this place. Crossing the Rui River eastward, one finds the Jingchuan public sports field, located in a willow grove by the water, with beautiful scenery. Passing the field is the west gate of Jingcheng. The road is not yet open to traffic, and only the city defense soldiers (belonging to the 61st Division) can be seen, holding sharp scissors to wait for the locals. When they encounter someone with a queue, they laugh and cut it off, saying, "It's been how many years of the Republic, and you still haven't cut your queue!" If someone is unwilling to cut it, the officials politely persuade them, and eventually they cut it off as well. It is said that several hundred queues are cut off daily in the four cities. The custom of keeping queues is even more prevalent in the west than in the east. If this practice can be followed, the backward custom can be eliminated. Jingcheng is strategically important. During the confrontation between the Song Dynasty and Western Xia, and during Zuo Zongtang's suppression of the Tongzhi Rebellion, it served as a base. It was also at Jingzhou Slope east of the city that Guo Ziyi single-handedly met with the Uyghur chieftain.

Leaving Jingcheng to the east, newly planted roadside willows, barely thick enough to encircle with one's hands, are lovely. Since Wating, the road has run alongside the Jing River, with cave dwellings visible on the mountains on both sides. Suddenly, the road veers away from the river, winding uphill to a flat plateau. We passed through a narrow road with deep pits and sheer cliffs, just wide enough for one vehicle to pass. Although there were protective walls on both sides, they seemed bottomless, causing anxiety. Twenty-two kilometers away is Gaozhen, and fourteen kilometers further is Yaodian, both small towns in Jingchuan where food and lodging are available. The border of Gansu Province ends at Yaodian. From Lanzhou to here, the total distance is more than four hundred and ninety kilometers. The mountains are layered and the road winds and turns, and it rained, so it took four and a half days to travel. Thirty li east of Yaodian, we entered the territory of Shaanxi and arrived at Changwu City. It was already dusk, and we stayed at the West Gate. We visited the county magistrate, Dang Bohu. According to him, the county covers an area of seventy li from east to west and eighty li from north to south, totaling more than fifty thousand square li, mostly plains. The county government collects a total of twenty-four thousand yuan in regular and additional taxes annually. The Jing River can naturally irrigate a portion of the fields, and the Guangren Canal can also irrigate more than five hundred mu. One landlord owns fifteen qing of land, and about thirty families own five or six qing, while the rest own dozens of mu. Tenant farmers account for only ten percent of the population, so there are few disputes over rent. The agricultural products are wheat and miscellaneous grains. Animal husbandry is also practiced on the slopes. There is a surplus of miscellaneous grains for self-sufficiency, but not enough wheat. It is commonly said that the surplus grain can be transported to Qianzhou and Liquan, but in reality, it is imported from Lingtai and Jingchuan in Gansu. Shaanxi Province is implementing a smoking ban, dividing the area into zones with deadlines. Changyi is scheduled to ban it completely by the end of this year. Cotton cultivation was first promoted last year, with good results. Sideline occupations for farmers include raising pigs and sheep. They drive them to Li Quan in herds of a hundred or more. The three types of wood – poplar, ailanthus, and tung – are also exported to other counties annually. In the early years of the Republic, Japanese merchants came to Chang in droves to buy tung wood specifically for making wooden clogs. In terms of school education, there is one higher primary school with more than seventy students, eighty-one primary schools with a total of more than two thousand four hundred students, and one private Zhaoren Primary School, founded by the county magistrate and various bureau chiefs, who also serve as teachers and are quite spirited. The people are simple and honest, but the atmosphere is not open. Foot binding for women and queue-keeping for men are common in the countryside. It is said that these customs will be thoroughly eliminated after the reorganization of the Baojia system.

The city is three li in circumference, with a moat about three zhang deep. To the southeast is an open plain, and to the northwest is a large valley. Therefore, there is a moat to the southeast but not to the northwest. There is a spring in the north city, emerging from under the city wall, which never dries up even in extreme drought. It is called Xiushui, and residents draw water from it. Although Changwu has a small population and lacks commercial prosperity, Shaanxi's tax collection agencies and highway stations are located here. Whenever there is trouble in the Central Plains, it is easily captured and becomes a battlefield. The Tang Dynasty established Zhaoren Temple to commemorate the fallen soldiers. Li Hua wrote an essay lamenting the ancient battlefields, and Ran Dian Town, where the Shaanxi-Gansu armies fought fiercely during the Xinhai Revolution, is also located in the county. At the end of January this spring, a group led by Liu Zidan suddenly led hundreds of cavalry to attack the county seat. County Magistrate Dang led the militia in street fighting for two hours before repelling them. Fortunately, the area was not devastated. Changwu is located on a plateau and is a vital point for transportation between Shaanxi and Gansu. As the saying goes, it is a place that must be contested for both offense and defense, as it has been throughout history.

The living conditions of the people are slightly better than in Gansu, as the Central Army was stationed here earlier and did not arbitrarily impose corvée and taxes like the mixed troops in Gansu. The tobacco tax of ten yuan per mu (last year, Chang County collected more than fourteen thousand yuan, all of which was handed over to the Shaanxi Provincial Tobacco Prohibition Committee) is paid by those who have obtained permits and actually cultivate tobacco. This is different from Gansu and Ningxia provinces, where taxes are levied on a per-mu basis regardless of whether tobacco is cultivated or not, causing farmers to lament that their land is a burden. In Chang County, one yuan can buy fifty jin of wheat flour, five or six jin of meat, and ten jin of salt. Most people can afford wheat flour, but fewer than one in a hundred can afford meat. Even having salt to eat and wearing cotton clothes in winter is only possible for half of the population. Boys and girls aged thirteen or fourteen are almost entirely without trousers. However, this situation is not unique to one place. Almost all rural areas affected by foreign economic invasion and domestic natural and man-made disasters are facing a tragic scene of hunger and cold.

May 2nd: Jing-Wu Railway Opens to Traffic; Fourth-Class Cars to Open First on April 21st; Connection with Jing-Hu Railway within Three Months 90

Wuhu Dispatch: The Jing-Wu Railway, built by the Jiangnan Railway Company, has been actively rushed to completion. Due to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's telegram ordering that it be connected to the Jing-Hu Railway within three months, the track laying work for the entire line has now reached the outskirts of Beijing. In addition to the section between Wuhu and Dangtu, which was opened to traffic and passengers on March 22nd, it has now been decided to open direct fourth-class passenger cars on the entire Jing-Wu line on the 21st of this month to facilitate passengers and merchants. There will be four round trips per day. However, due to the new construction, the roadbed may not be completely stable, so the travel time will be slightly extended to four hours. Once the ballast is thickened, the speed will be increased, and it will take about two and a half hours. The fare for the entire fourth-class trip is set at seven corners, which is only a quarter of the price of 2.60 yuan for a long-distance bus on the Jing-Wu highway. The Jing-Wu Motor Transport Company will suffer a major blow as a result. In order to maintain its business, the company has obtained approval from the Jiangsu and Anhui provincial construction departments to reduce fares at all stations along the line by 30% from April 21st. However, with more frequent bus services, it may still be able to survive. The thirteen new locomotives ordered by the Jiangnan Company in England have already arrived in Shanghai, and the first, second, and third class passenger cars ordered in Shanghai will be shipped to Wuhu soon. Therefore, it is scheduled to open all classes of passenger cars on May 2nd. The Nanjing connection station has been selected at Honghuadi (i.e., Guanyin'an), and construction is planned. In Beijing, three branch stations will be set up at Zhonghuamen, Xinjiekou, and Xiaguan. As for the issue of connecting with the Jing-Hu Railway, personnel have been dispatched to Beijing to negotiate, and it should be possible to meet the deadline within three months. It is decided that a test run will be held tomorrow (the 19th). A special train will depart from Wuhu at 11:00 a.m., arriving at Zhonghuamen in Beijing at approximately 3:00 p.m. It will then be tested on the return trip to Wuhu that day. In addition, the Wuhu-Xuan and Xuan-Sun sections of the company have long been officially open to traffic. As it is now the time when tea from the Xuanhui area is being marketed, the number of merchants transporting tea to North China is the highest. In the past, transportation was inconvenient, and the export of Hui tea was extremely difficult and expensive. In order to facilitate tea merchants, special joint transportation arrangements have been made with the Jing-Hu and Pu-Jin lines. Tea merchants are spared the trouble of transshipment midway, and the cost savings are even greater, which is welcomed by all. Several thousand merchants have already delivered tea in recent days. Before the Jing-Wu section is officially open to traffic, tea will be transported to Dangtu and then by bus. However, in a week, Sunjiabu to Nanjing will be completely directly accessible. (18th)

Jingdezhen: Abolition of Kiln Prohibition in the Porcelain Industry 92

Jingdezhen is one of China's four famous towns, and its main product is porcelain. At the same time, it is known throughout the world for its porcelain and once occupied the most glorious and indelible page in the history of world industry. This cannot be denied by people all over the world. However, in recent years, it has completely lost its former glory and entered a path of decline and decay. The reasons for its failure are due to objective circumstances, but also to the conservatism of the workers, who do not know how to improve, the division of factions, and the failure to merge, and ignorance of the world trend. Among the various bad habits, the prohibition of opening a kiln is the biggest obstacle to improving the ceramic industry. Therefore, in order to develop the ceramic industry in Jiangxi Province, the Jiangxi authorities have specially established a Pottery Industry Administration in Jingdezhen to revitalize the dream of the pottery industry and commissioned Du Chongyuan, an expert in the porcelain industry, to preside over the improvement matters. In Du's plan, the first step is to abolish the "kiln prohibition," which has been the biggest obstacle to the ceramic industry for the past forty years.

The beginning of the kiln prohibition dates back to the Guangxu period of the late Qing Dynasty. At that time, kiln owners (i.e., those who opened kiln factories) sacrificed the interests of other businesses for their own benefit, and gathered their peers to jointly formulate this self-defeating suicide policy. From then on, kiln owners only managed the firing of the kiln, and did not care whether the porcelain was good or bad after firing. If there was under-firing (meaning not cooked), over-firing (meaning overcooked), or collapse, the kiln owners not only did not bear the responsibility for compensation, but also had to ask the kiln owners for firewood costs. Kiln owners were not allowed to express dissatisfaction. Otherwise, the next time they fired, they would deliberately damage the porcelain to blackmail them. Because kiln owners were unable to fire themselves, they still had to entrust them to fire for them. Otherwise, the kiln owners would unanimously refuse. The suffering of the kiln owners was great and extreme. In recent years, there have been many incidents of collapse. The main reason is that the kiln owners only care about the quantity of goods, so they have expanded the kiln body (twice as large as before), but they do not know that after the kiln body is enlarged, the sagger (a refractory container used to hold porcelain in the kiln) becomes heavier. At the same time, the firepower is increased. When the firepower is strong and the sagger is heavy, there is often a danger of the kiln collapsing.

This corrupt habit has been around for a long time and is not easy to eradicate. When Du Chongyuan took office, in order to be cautious, he convened various businesses and explained them in detail, resolutely abolishing the prohibition and issuing a notice. The notice said, "Jingdezhen's porcelain industry has a long history and is famous at home and abroad. However, because the work is conservative, unchangeable, and divided into factions, the glorious history and vast sales market of thousands of years have been taken away by foreign porcelain, which is extremely painful. The director of this bureau has insight into the accumulated abuses and is determined to eliminate bad habits and improve the Chinese porcelain industry. Since arriving in Zhen, I have carefully studied and realized that the biggest of the bad rules is the prohibition of opening a kiln. Once a kiln is prohibited, the number of damaged products in the damaged area increases, making it impossible to work. Porcelain merchants lack goods to purchase and can only sit and wait, which hinders production internally and loses reputation externally. In addition, the volume of the kiln body has been enlarged, and there are many cases of collapse. The number of firings has been reduced, and the cost must be huge. Over time, the kiln owners will be in deficit and the porcelain merchants will be insufficient, and they will inevitably perish together. The management of pottery affairs by this bureau is primarily to promote benefits and eliminate abuses. From now on, the kiln prohibition will be permanently abolished. No one is allowed to comply in appearance but disobey in reality, or to continue the accumulated habits of the past, lest they offend. Comply immediately, this is the notice." In the future, the bureau also plans to organize the Jiangxi Pottery Industry Improvement Committee and the Pottery Workers Affairs Improvement Committee, whose main members are all local people who are enthusiastic about improving the pottery industry and workers with experience, and they will be combined. The opportunity for improvement is not far away, and we should wait and see.

Jiangxi Province Expands Agricultural Loans — Provincial Government is Currently Deploying Implementation — 93

Nanchang Dispatch: Jiangxi suffered from eight years of banditry and the unprecedented drought last year. The countryside is fragmented and desolate. Not only have people gone bankrupt, but the banditry was most tragic in southern Jiangxi and the secluded areas bordering neighboring provinces. The disaster areas are of course unable to resume spring plowing. Even in the hinterland near the provincial capital and eastern Jiangxi, which were formerly known as rich areas, farmers have no food grains or seeds and cannot maintain their livelihoods. In order to save the countryside, the provincial government recently convened the directors of the agricultural college, Dong Shijin, and others to discuss relief measures. After the Closing of the Mouth: A Glimpse of the Current Situation in Guantai: Rising Water and Wind Blow the Main Current Back to the River; Height of the Jinmenkou is Level with the Two Dams 94

Kaifeng Dispatch: The Guantai closing project is of great importance to the lives and property of the people of Henan, Shandong, and Hebei provinces. On the 11th, Bianyuan suddenly received a report from Kong Xiangrong that it had been closed. All parties felt surprised. On the 12th, the reporter went to the Work Relief Group to inquire. Because its important staff were all at the construction site, the details were not clear. In order to understand the situation, I personally went to inspect at 11:00 a.m. today. Those who accompanied me were Zheng Kanghou, the magistrate of Kaifeng County. The car left Caomen, crossed the moat embankment, and drove along the Kai-Cao Road. Passing through the fifth district of Kaifeng, the wheat fields were green and endless. Compared with the sixth, seventh, and eighth districts, where the land was covered with yellow sand and people had nothing to live on except planting willows and peanuts, the difference was like heaven and earth. After Zhaotaoying, about forty li from Zhizhi, we entered the jurisdiction of Chenliu County. After another twenty li to Quxingji, we turned north for a li or so, passed Guantai, and drove more than ten li into the beach to reach the Chenliu ferry. On the south bank, stones were transported from the Lanfeng Station, and thousands of large and small carts carrying willow branches and straw from Kaifeng, Lanfeng, Minquan, Chenliu, and other counties came and went endlessly. The unloaded piles of willow straw were like mountains. Many boats transported materials from the river to the north bank. The materials on the north bank were even more numerous. The iron anchor alone was amazing. Walking east along the bank for dozens of steps, there was a water-permeable willow dam, and the degree of siltation had reached nine points. In front of it was another dam, which was similar in shape. These two dams were both built on the mouth last month on the 27th and 28th. Because of their effect, the main current moved south. Climbing the earthen embankment to the north, the supervisors, soldiers, and Maofu, and the disaster victims' teams from Kaifeng, Lanfeng, Dongming, Changyuan, Fengqiu Puyang, Hua County, etc., totaled about more than two thousand people. Those who pushed the soil and those who carried the materials came and went like a shuttle. Some were raising and thickening the earthen embankment, preparing to protect the eaves with willow branches at the appropriate time. It was heard from the supervisors that they would build it three meters high and one zhang and five wide. When the entire embankment is completed, it will take more than a day. Going east to Longmenkou, Kong Xiangrong and Secretary Xu Shihao, Inspector Zhu Changan, Yao Zeton, and Huanglihui engineer Zheng Yaoxi were all engaged in supervision. Ma River's current trended east, opening its mouth due east. Originally, there was no water. After the 20th, the peach blossom water rose, and the northwest wind blew strongly, gradually washing away, eventually causing the main current to flow east and return to the main river. This was the main reason for the rapid closing of the mouth. The current height of Jinmenkou has been built to the same level as the east and west dams, forming a unified whole. Because it is blocked with willow and stone bags, a closing willow broom is being added on the side facing the river to completely seal off the air. According to measurements, the water surface of the mouth facing the river is five feet higher than the water surface behind the river. The Huayang embankment on the back river originally had a river surface one kilometer wide and about four meters deep. Now the water surface is only about thirty meters wide, and the water depth is less than one meter, and the siltation is very fast. The disaster areas of Changyuan and Kaifeng have both reported a five-foot drop in water level and will soon be dry. According to Kong Xiangrong, since the Work Relief Group took over the closing of the mouth on the 21st of last month, they have tried their best to concentrate materials and manpower and proceed accordingly. First, they rushed to build the eave protection project on the east and west dams previously built in a short period of time, that is, willow bundles and stone piles were placed along the river on both dams, and the two ends were sunk with ropes to make them come out of the water, and then stones were thrown, or the rear section was staked and stoned to make them quite solid and without worries. At the bottom of the kernel willow stone pillow, the rope was tied to the boat in front of the dam, and the boat was fixed with an iron anchor. Willow stone pillows were made on the boat, the stones were wrapped in willow lead wire, and the waist was tied with hemp rope to make the length the same as the mouth and strong. Then they were slowly sent down from the two boats to sink to the bottom. Then another layer was lowered to make it silt up. Day and night, a total of 419 pillows were dropped in the mouth of the two main dams before the closure was successful, 374 facing the river, 84 behind the river, and 246 on the edge of the back river. 350 pillows were dropped in the mouth of the East Dam, 949 facing the river, and 226 on the edge of the back river, for a total of 2,648 pillows, which was very effective. When it reached a considerable level, more than ten feet from the water surface, personnel, soldiers, laborers, materials, and materials were gathered before dawn on the 11th to start rushing to block, and it was successful. As of the 11th of this month, about 3.5 million jin of willow branches, about 1,800 market squares of stone, about 1.3 million jin of straw, about 88,000 sacks, about 191,000 jin of hemp, and about 810 bundles of lead wire were used, which was much more than the budget. The remaining materials will be handed over to the future protective agencies, etc. About half a li northwest of the mouth, a play was being performed. Then I went to the office of the Work Relief Group to rest for a while. At seven o'clock, I braved the rain to cross the river and return. It was already ten o'clock when I returned to the juice. (13th)

Eastern Zhejiang: Lifting of the Blockade of Quzhou Territory - No Trace of Bandits on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Border 96

Quzhou Dispatch: The counties of Jiangshan, Changshan, and Kaihua in Quzhou territory, Eastern Zhejiang, are adjacent to Wuyuan, Yushan, and Dexing in Jiangxi province. Previously, due to the occupation of the bandit rebels in the Eastern Jiangxi area, in order to cut off their material supplies, these counties strictly blockaded and uniformly prohibited the transportation of goods into Jiangxi. Even the few law-abiding citizens were only allowed to purchase necessary items like salt and kerosene based on their good citizen certificates, and even then, restrictions were imposed to prevent them from flowing into the bandit areas. After the implementation of this policy, the annual business of trade goods transported from Jiangshan, Changshan, and Kaihua to Eastern Jiangxi decreased from over 1.2 million yuan to over 100,000 yuan, causing a huge impact on the local economy and losses to merchants. It is now known that Chairman Huang of the Provincial Government, considering that the bandit disturbances in Jiangxi have been suppressed, recently sent Lu Zhongxiu, the Chief of the Third Branch of the Security Preservation Division, to participate in the post-bandit conference held by the Border Area Pacification Headquarters of the four provinces, to discuss this matter. It was decided that since the local bandit disturbances have been quelled, the blockade of the bandit areas will be lifted starting this month, so that goods from Jiangshan, Changshan, Kaihua, and other counties can be freely transported and sold into Jiangxi, in order to benefit the merchants and help revive the local economy. The border defenses at present are quite solid, and no trace of bandits has been discovered. However, in the eastern countryside of Wuyuan, bordering Kaihua and Kunlian, scattered bandits have been entering from Fuliang and Anhui in the past two weeks, hoping to regroup in Jiangxi. The Zhejiang garrison is strictly preventing and suppressing them, so that the ashes of the bandit rebellion will not rekindle.

Zhejiang Youth Commits Suicide in Hotel 101

At around 4:00 PM on the 18th, a traveler wearing a brocade crepe cotton robe checked into the Railway Hotel on Chezhan Road. He claimed to be named Shen Jikang, 25 years old, from Zhejiang. He immediately booked room number seven to rest. He went out at around 6:00 PM and returned to the hotel at 10:00 PM, closed the door, and went to sleep. Unexpectedly, at 4:15 AM yesterday morning, the hotel tea boy heard moaning from the room. When he called out, there was no response. Knowing something was wrong, he immediately opened the door and entered. He saw Jikang with a pale face, knowing that he had taken poison. He immediately reported the information to the front desk, who carried him to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. However, due to the severe overdose, he died at around 9:00 AM. The local head of the police station, Xi Jiliang, has already reported to the local branch court, and at around 3:00 PM in the afternoon, Prosecutor Shen went to conduct an autopsy, confirming that he had died from poisoning. Since he had no family, the neighborhood chief prepared a coffin for burial.

Boat capsizes outside the river, Nineteen Deaths 105

In the river of Hupu, our county, there are often ships sailing to and from various ports, carrying cargo. In the first ten days of this month, there was a ship named Gongda that was commissioned to carry bean cakes to Haizhou. However, ships leaving the port are usually loaded with local products for sale before loading goods for the return trip. The Gongda ship, because the owner was poor, was already mortgaged to a bank in the city for 20,000 yuan and lacked the funds to load goods, so it left the port empty. There were five other ships traveling with it, but they were all heavily loaded. Unexpectedly, when the ships were near the Menshan area near Haizhou, they suddenly encountered a hurricane. Because the Gongda was an empty ship, it could not withstand the storm and immediately capsized. The shipowner Jiang Dashi (from Hengjing, Taicang) and nineteen of his companions were all drowned without any survivors. An elder named Zhu has already arrived at the port to report the incident. The total loss of the entire ship is estimated to be around 40,000 yuan.

Yangzhou: Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau Expedites Closure 106

The Jiangdu Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Bureau, having been ordered to merge with the Jiangdu Business Tax Bureau and handle its duties concurrently, it is now known that the bureau has already expedited its closure after transferring the seals and licenses in accordance with provincial orders. Regarding the spring tax payments, it has already received an order from the provincial government to prepare a list and report it. At the same time, it is taking the spring taxes that have already been collected to the provincial bureau for settlement. It is reported that after Bureau Chief Qin of the bureau received the order, he not only ordered the tax collectors in various rural districts to expedite the closure of the spring tax payments, but is now also rushing to handle all the procedures day and night, so that it can be closed as soon as possible.

Zhenjiang: Training Police Dogs to Assist in Investigations 107

The Provincial Tobacco Prohibition Association, in order to assist in investigative work, has established a police dog training group, hiring Dong Hanliang as the director. The group has one German Shepherd and one foreign breed old dog, and the rest are domestic breeds, totaling over ten dogs. Only six meet the training standards. Basic training will be completed by the end of this month, and application training will begin immediately. After another two months, they will be fully trained. After the completion of the training, investigators will lead them to work at the stations and ports, conducting investigations. If it is effective, it will be promoted to various counties.

Construction Department Reprimands Electric Light Company 108

The street light donation in the provincial capital has always been collected by the Public Security Bureau on a household basis and handed over to the Electric Light Company. When Zhong Zhiying was the director of the Construction Bureau, he and the Public Security Bureau jointly formulated a rectification plan, intending to change it to a 5% surcharge on the monthly electricity bill for citizens. However, it could not be implemented due to obstacles. Last year, the county government was ordered to rectify the street lights in the provincial capital, and it was planned to implement the previously established plan. The only question was whether users would be willing to pay this donation. Therefore, the Electric Light Company, the Public Security Bureau, and the Construction Bureau were called together for discussion. It was decided that the company should first issue a notice to solicit users' opinions before making a decision. However, the Electric Light Company was eager to implement it and did not hesitate to submit a report to the Construction Department, stating that after the meeting, it was decided that the company would submit a request to the Construction Department to forward it to the Construction Committee, so that the revised collection plan and regulations could be approved and then announced for implementation. The Construction Department then ordered the Zhenjiang County government to reply. The county government recorded the agreed-upon method and submitted it to the Construction Department. After receiving the report, the Construction Department issued an order to the county government yesterday, stating that the submitted documents had been noted. The company had changed the agreed-upon method of the meeting on its own and submitted a report to the department, which was extremely absurd and has been reprimanded. It has also been instructed to proceed according to the county's meeting decision, which should be noted.

Nanjing: Porcelain Merchants Petition for the Abolition of Miscellaneous Taxes 109

The porcelain merchants of various ports, opposing Jingdezhen's illegal establishment of a porcelain liquidation donation, have repeatedly consulted and petitioned for its abolition, as reported in the newspapers. It is now known that porcelain merchants from Nanjing, Shanghai, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Changzhou, Nantong, Jiujiang, Hankou, and other ports have jointly petitioned the relevant authorities to abolish it and have sent representatives Wang Shoushan, Yuan Shouchun, Hu Gan, Cheng Zhang Diqian, Yan Qing, and Hu Aigu to the Chairman's Headquarters and the Jiangxi Provincial Government to request relief. The memorandum to Chairman Chiang from the representatives states that the recent revival of the porcelain donation in Jingdezhen contradicts the central government's decree to abolish likin and other donations, the decision of the Second National Financial Conference to abolish miscellaneous taxes within a limited time, and the Jiangxi Provincial Finance Department's approval in document No. 2243 of the 21st year of the Republic, granting porcelain taxes the same treatment as other taxes. The merchants dare to petition for abolition because their leader is advocating the National Economic Construction Movement, the initial step of which is to eliminate exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies and alleviate the suffering of the people. This proves that the porcelain liquidation donation should not be allowed to exist under any circumstances. Moreover, the quota for the donation is 169,000 yuan, and the amount collected has already reached over 100,000 yuan. The remaining 39,000 yuan is a drop in the bucket and cannot compensate for the larger plan. It only harms the law and discipline. If it is allowed to continue indefinitely without being abolished, it is like drinking poison to quench thirst. Therefore, they urgently petition for an order to abolish it, and so on.

The squad leader training class for the security teams of the six counties of Nantong, Rugao, Chongming, Hai'an, Qidong, and Jingjiang in the Nantong district held a graduation ceremony on the 18th. Zheng Yitong, the district security commander, encouraged all the trainees to be determined to fight in the future and not be changed by the environment, as if they had not been trained. In the afternoon, Director Xiang and staff member Yu Cheng visited Langshan. On the morning of the 19th, they returned to Zhenjiang on the Boxian warship.

Haimen: Disturbance by Smokers at the Second Opium Treatment Branch 113

The County Opium Treatment Center, due to the large number of opium addicts being treated, was unable to accommodate them. Therefore, the first branch was established in the remaining rooms of the first district office, and the second branch was established in the Zhongshan Hall. The center transferred the opium addicts from the first branch to the second branch the day before yesterday (the 16th) for the convenience of management. Yesterday (the 17th) afternoon, opium addicts Zhu Xiangxian, He Benkun, and others, complaining that the treatment at the second branch was inadequate, demanded to be transferred to the main center from Director Zhang Yanqiang. When their request was not granted, the opium addicts stirred up a commotion, causing great disorder. Director Zhang reported to the County Opium Prohibition Committee, which dispatched several members of the security team to suppress the disturbance, and it gradually subsided.

Opium Prohibition Committee Strictly Detains Smokers Who Refuse to Report 114

Since the County Opium Prohibition Committee began conducting opium prohibition and treatment, it has been through four batches. However, a number of opium addicts who were notified have refused to report, including sixteen in the first batch, twenty in the second batch, forty-one in the third batch, and sixty-two in the fourth batch, totaling one hundred and thirty-nine people. The committee believes that these opium addicts are disregarding the law and watching with suspicion, which is detrimental to the opium prohibition policy. Yesterday, it specially prepared a list and ordered the district offices and public security bureaus to instruct the police to arrest and escort them.

Hangzhou: Emergency Repair of Dangerous River Embankments Along the Qiantang River 115

The recent continuous spring rains have caused the Qiantang River to rise sharply. Yesterday, the water level reached eight meters. The beach at the Qin Yin Tang area on the north bank has been eroded by water for over two hundred feet, and the situation is quite dangerous. The Construction Department has ordered the Water Conservancy Bureau to work with the municipal government to devise a method to urgently repair the water diversion dam that has been damaged by the river, in order to control the water flow. It is estimated that over 63,000 yuan will be needed, with each of the two organizations contributing half. Construction will begin on a set date. In addition, hundreds of thousands of mu of newly formed sand land have recently risen above the Qibao area on the Hangzhou-Hai'ning embankment. This can be used to protect the embankment and construct a water dam. The Qiantang River tide has changed direction due to the rise of sand and is now surging fiercely towards Nansha, Xiaoshan. In the future, those who want to watch the tide at Hai'ning will have to change their location.

Cotton Farmers Oppose Improved Cotton 116

The Zhejiang Construction Department received a telegram from the Yuyao county magistrate, reporting that in the Xinpu coastal area of the county, after designating 10,000 mu of land to promote improved cotton, when Zhang Ming, the chief of the Construction Section, went to the countryside to gather various cotton farmers, a farmer named Pan Yaozhang gathered thousands of people to surround Zhang and others, and set fire to the cotton area office. After receiving the report, the provincial government has ordered the county magistrate to strictly arrest the ringleaders and prosecute them according to law.

Security Preservation Department Executes Red Pill Trafficker 117

The Zhejiang Provincial Security Preservation Department, based on the report from the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, arrested Ye Qing, who had been trafficking in red pills, and the report was found to be true. He was sentenced to death and executed by firing squad at the previously selected execution ground at 9:00 AM yesterday.

All preparations are now complete, and it has been decided to start today. All lecturers will be mobilized to go to the countryside in Wusong, Jiangwan, and other places to give lectures. At the same time, agricultural films will be shown, or farmers' gatherings will be held, to attract farmers to participate and promote legitimate entertainment for farmers. U.S. Economic Survey Mission Reception Office Yesterday Sent Letters to Various Organizations Regarding Participation in the Reception and Notification of Representatives' Names 123

The U.S. Far East Economic Survey Mission arrived in China yesterday aboard the Dollar Line's President Harrison from Japan. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai at 8:00 AM on the 22nd, docking at the Dollar Line Wharf in Pudong. The reception office for the U.S. Economic Survey Mission, jointly organized by various circles in Shanghai, sent letters to various organizations yesterday, stating: "Regarding the U.S. Economic Survey Mission, it departed for China on March 22nd and will arrive in Shanghai on April 22nd to exchange opinions with leaders from various circles in China. In May, the mission will divide into groups to conduct inspections in Guangzhou, Wuhan, Pingjin, and other places, returning to Shanghai in about three weeks and departing for the United States on June 14th. The mission members and their families total about 26 people, all of whom are leaders from various circles in the United States. The purpose of their inspection is to understand the actual situation of China's construction and the conditions of the Far East market, to determine how to cooperate with China, and to make suggestions to their government. The China International Trade Association, the China Branch of the International Chamber of Commerce, and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, considering the importance of the mission and its close relationship with the Party and the country, have specially initiated the organization of a reception office, and have set up an office in the International Hotel, responsible for planning all reception matters. After the mission arrives in Shanghai, it will be welcomed by various organizations in Shanghai. It is assumed that your association is also happy to participate in the reception. Please immediately appoint three representatives and notify our office of their names for contact."

The reception office invited various organizations in Shanghai to send three representatives to participate. As of yesterday, the organizations that have responded and confirmed their participation include: Shanghai Bankers Association (representatives: Ju Songsun, Xu Xinliu, Chen Zheqing), Shanghai Native Bankers Association (representatives: Yu Zuoting, Wang Huailian, Xi Jiming), Shanghai Local Self-Government Association (representatives: Mu Ouchu, Xu Xinliu, Liu Hongsheng), China Aviation Association (representatives: Wang Xiaolai, Wang Rutang, Yao Xijiu), China National Roads Association (representative: Fan Zhenchu), International Affairs Research Association (representatives: Nie Lusheng, Liu Zhanen, Zhang Xianglin), American Returned Students Association (representatives: Cao Yunxiang, Zhang Sixu, Li Bingrui), Shanghai YMCA (representatives: Lu Ganchen, Yang Yihui, Wang Chuntao), Pacific Institute (representative: Chen Liting), World's Chinese Students' Federation (representatives: Zhu Shaoping, Zhang Guoliang, Wu Deyun), Chinese Institute of Engineers (representatives: Xu Peihuang, Xu Shanxiang, Wang Shengshan). The representatives of four organizations, including the Chinese Industrial Associations, Shanghai Timber Traders Association, Chinese Economic Society, and the Chinese Women's Association, have not yet been determined. In total, there are fifteen organizations participating in the welcome. The survey mission reception office has leased four rooms on the fourth floor of the International Hotel and has been working very hard in recent days to handle various tasks. In order to gather more ideas, in addition to the official list released yesterday, Li Zufa, Shen Kunshan, Zou Bingwen, Nie Lusheng, and four others have been additionally appointed as members of the proposal group. The reception office, considering the imminent arrival of the survey mission in Shanghai, held a full executive committee meeting last night at the International Hotel to discuss all the ongoing matters.

Mortgage Loans to Be Managed by Three Banks, Credit Loans to Be Handled in Conjunction with the Bankers' Association 129
