It is learned that the three banks are currently discussing detailed measures for implementation. It is also reported that the Ministry of Finance stipulated that the mortgage loan of 15 million yuan will be managed by the three banks, as the increase in capital of the three banks this time is for loan relief to industry and commerce and to stabilize the social economy. As for the remaining credit guarantee loan of 5 million yuan, it will be handled by the three banks in conjunction with the Bankers' Association. In response to the requests of the Chamber of Commerce and other organizations, the Bankers' Association had previously established a sub-committee to discuss measures, and 1.885 million yuan had already been recognized by the member banks. Therefore, the Bankers' Association decided to join in the handling after the three banks have agreed on the measures. If the funds are insufficient, whether the Central Bank will underwrite or whether the banks will re-recognize will depend on the outcome of the three banks' discussions. In the future, a committee will be organized to preside over the matter.

Zhejiang Province Borrows 2 Million Yuan, Contract Can Be Signed Immediately, Loan Will Be Borne by Banks Including Bank of China and Farmers Bank, Interest at 9%, Principal and Interest to Be Fully Repaid in Three Years 130

Xu Qingfu, Director of the Finance Department of Zhejiang Province, considering that various construction projects in the province urgently need to continue, has specially continued to use 3.6 million in the face value of the 23rd-year construction bonds to borrow 2 million from banks including the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications for work relief. The draft contract has been agreed upon with the branches in Hangzhou, and the branches have sent it to Shanghai for instructions from the head office. Once the head office approves it, it can be formally signed and the funds can be started. The loan includes 200,000 from the Central Bank, 300,000 from the China Farmers Bank, and the remaining 1.5 million will be recognized by banks including the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Xingye Bank, Jincheng Bank, Salt Industry Bank, Zhongnan Bank, and Dalu Bank. The interest rate is set at 9%, with interest paid at the end of March and September each year. The principal and interest will be repaid in three years, starting from the end of February of the 26th year of the Republic of China and repaying the principal monthly until the end of February of the 29th year of the Republic of China when the principal and interest will be fully repaid.

According to Xinsheng News Agency, the 19th session of the International Labor Conference will open in Geneva on June 4th. It is scheduled to leave for Nanjing next Tuesday to pay a visit to the authorities and handle passport and other formalities. A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency also learned that the agenda of this conference has been decided by the 68th and 69th meetings of the Council of the International Labor Organization, including the following seven items: (1) The issue of maintaining the due and vested rights of disability, old age, and widowhood insurance for workers moving from one country to another; (2) The issue of prohibiting women from engaging in various underground mining work; (3) The issue of youth unemployment; (4) The issue of labor recruitment in colonies and areas with similar labor conditions; (5) The issue of wage payment during holidays; (6) The issue of reducing working hours; (7) The issue of revising the convention on limiting the working hours of coal miners.

Art Exhibition, 12th Day of Preview, Various Schools Request Preferential Visits 133

According to the Central News Agency, yesterday (the 19th) was the 12th day of the Shanghai preview of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London. People from all walks of life have been visiting in recent days. Because the exhibits have unparalleled artistic value and are systematically arranged, they are very convenient for research, so they have been well received. The number of visitors yesterday was even greater, and many were from the art world. They were very interested in each exhibit and lingered for a long time before leaving, which shows the depth of art's appeal to people. The news obtained yesterday is recorded as follows:

Art Circles Discuss Photographing Mr. Shiwei

The Shanghai Fine Arts Life Magazine Society sent a letter to the association yesterday, saying: "We aim to develop Chinese art and make it universal. We pay special attention to ancient Chinese art. Because your association will use ancient Chinese art to win glory for the country overseas, we are willing to do our best to promote it and plan to publish a special issue. We have specially sent Mr. Luo Guxun to contact you and hope that you will grant us permission to take photographs." This is addressed to the Chinese Art International Exhibition Association and signed by the Shanghai Fine Arts Life Magazine Society.

General Outline of Explanations of Calligraphy and Painting

The exhibits of this exhibition are divided into four parts: (1) Bronzes, (2) Porcelain, (3) Calligraphy and Painting, (4) Miscellaneous Items. Explanations of bronzes and porcelain have been stated in the catalog of exhibits for the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London sold by the association. The explanations of calligraphy and painting have also been written by the association. The first chapter of the explanation is recorded below for the reference of those who appreciate calligraphy and painting. The first chapter of the explanation says: "The study of Chinese calligraphy and painting has a very long history. Its characteristic lies in the mutual connection between the study of calligraphy and the study of painting, so it occupies an important position in world art. Only China has the study of painting and no study of calligraphy. Although Japan has the study of calligraphy, it takes the study of Chinese calligraphy as its study of calligraphy. Chinese calligraphy and painting are both based on the premise of expressing inner thoughts. There is a close connection between them, and there is no limit to each other. All the nobility of personality and the profoundness of knowledge are based on the spiritual expression, inner accumulation and external manifestation, which is different from simply depicting the entity of objects. The techniques are also sufficient to support it. The surviving relics of ancient objects (referring to silk and paper) such as Zhong Yao, Wang Xizhi, and Gu Kaizhi of the Six Dynasties are relatively old and difficult to determine their authenticity. Since the Tang and Song Dynasties, there are still many remaining, which are sufficient for research. Now, we will explore the sources and schools of calligraphy and painting of past dynasties and list them to introduce them to scholars at home and abroad who are interested in Chinese calligraphy and painting as follows." (The following is the evolution of the study of calligraphy in the second chapter and its famous artists will be continued tomorrow.)

Various Schools Request Preferential Treatment

The exhibits of this exhibition are rich in educational and artistic value. In recent days, various schools have sent letters requesting preferential visits, including Shanghai Law College, Jiangsu Provincial Songjiang Women's Middle School, Jiangsu Provincial Shanghai Middle School, Guanghua University, and Daxia University. Regarding Shanghai Law College, Guanghua University, Daxia University, and other schools, the association has replied to contact the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education directly regarding the preferential measures and the arrangement of visit dates. Regarding Jiangsu Provincial Songjiang Women's Middle School and Shanghai Middle School, the association has directly replied to approve them.

International Telecommunications Bureau Domestic and International Wireless Telephone Lines Can Be Opened for Calls Simultaneously by the End of the Year 134

According to the Central News Agency, after the equipment for the International Telecommunications Bureau's wireless radio station for opening international wireless telephone lines was shipped, it is being rushed to be installed, with the goal of completing the installation by the end of this month and connecting to various countries within the year. Domestic wireless telephones in Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Wuhan can also be opened for calls simultaneously. The details are recorded as follows:

All Reporting Machines Have Arrived, Installation to Be Completed by the End of the Month

The international wireless telephone reporting machines have been shipped to Shanghai one after another since the end of last year, and now they have all arrived and are being rushed to be installed. It is estimated that the installation can be completed by the end of this month. The countries to be connected include England, Germany, Italy, the Philippines, the United States, Japan, Saigon, Geneva, and other places. It is estimated that the calls can be fully opened within the year. If the reporting service is busy in the future, more equipment may be added. It is still possible to cope with the different times in Europe and the United States. The difficulty is in the Philippines and Japan, because the time is the same, and it is feared that the existing equipment will not be sufficient when the reporting service is busy.

Actively Contacting Various Countries to Connect for Calls

The contact with various countries for calls, the European countries and Japan, is handled by the Ministry of Communications. The United States and the Philippines are handled by the International Telecommunications Bureau. The timing of formal calls must be determined according to the outcome of the negotiations. The call price is determined by the Ministry of Communications. International calls are based on international standard prices, while the calculation of domestic and international transfer call costs is more complicated, so it is still being drafted.

Domestic Calls Will Be Fully Open by the End of the Year

As for domestic wireless telephone calls, Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Wuhan are all installing equipment, and it is estimated that it will also be completed by the end of this month or early next month. Formal calls must also be fully opened within this year. The northern areas can use wired telephones, so there is no need to install wireless telephones separately. When domestic and international telephones are fully opened at that time, China's telephone business will become more developed.

Measures for Dividing Accumulated Grain Funds and Properties in Shanghai County and Shanghai City 139

The issue of dividing the accumulated grain funds and properties and the original public funds and properties shared by Shanghai City and County has been re-evaluated by a joint evaluation committee of the city and county, and the committee members have conducted a thorough survey and assessment. It has long been estimated that the total value of all the bases, houses, and Shanghai Hospital equipment is 1,175,742.43 yuan. The association immediately convened a meeting of members to calculate and divide according to the original ratio of 63% for the city and 37% for the county. The decided measures have now been published and recorded as follows: (A) According to the public property valuation summary table, Shanghai Hospital, Changtai Wood Company, Duojia Road (outer section), and Tianhou Palace are allocated to the city, valued at 753,634.86 yuan. (B) According to the public property valuation summary table, Liangjie Xiaoci, Yeshi Garden, Chen Yuan Liang Gongci, Qiuzhi Academy, Duojia Road (middle and inner sections), Da Wang Temple, and Yimiao Dragon Boat Hall are allocated to the county, valued at 422,107.57 yuan. (C) The public property obtained by the city in item A, according to the ratio, exceeds 32,917.13 yuan, which should be returned to the county when the Tianhou Palace base and houses have operating production. (D) If any city and county public properties are discovered in the future, they should be divided according to this case. The above resolutions will be submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Jiangsu Provincial Government by the city's related bureaus and the Shanghai County Government for approval.

Zhejiang Province Cleans Up Drugs, Zhejiang Provincial Association Requests Extension of Two Years 142

The All Zhejiang Provincial Association wired the Zhejiang Provincial Government, saying: "To the esteemed Chairman Huang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government: The achievements of Zhejiang Province in banning opium are superior to those of other provinces. Since Chairman Lu presented to the Central Government for approval the Provisional Regulations for Cleaning Up Drugs in Zhejiang Province and selected and appointed special commissioners for opium suppression to go to various counties to conduct on-site investigations, the results have been increasingly remarkable. However, it is found that in Article 2 of the newly promulgated Measures for Opium Suppression, Zhejiang Province has been listed as an absolutely prohibited province for planting. Article 4 deals with cracking down on opium smokers, organizing opium smoker registration, and collectively referring to provinces and cities. Article 6 allows for the purchase of opium from border provinces, and Article 7 allows for the establishment of opium shops in various provinces and cities, all of which restore the opium suppression measures of the late Qing Dynasty. This method of restricting and collecting opium is a good method for provinces where opium addiction is rampant, but from the perspective of Zhejiang Province, where opium suppression has always been strict, having opium smoker licenses and opium shops in operation is tantamount to the revival of opium and the spread of opium disasters. Opium has spread for more than a century, and because Zhejiang is close to Shanghai, with convenient land and water transportation, private smuggling is easy, and secret private smoking has not been completely eliminated. However, according to the special article of the criminal law punishing people for opium smoking, those who commit the crime must be punished. Openly selling and smoking opium is absolutely impossible. Therefore, the measures for implementing opium suppression may be feasible in other provinces, but they are not feasible in our Zhejiang. Recently, rumors have spread in Shanghai that someone has recognized to run opium shops in Zhejiang Province for 2.5 million yuan. In the past, those who were executed for private sales were numerous. If opium is allowed to be sold openly now, what kind of government system will it be? This saying is probably a rumor. Furthermore, Article 1 of the Measures for Implementing Opium Suppression stipulates that in addition to handling according to other opium suppression regulations, the existing Regulations for Cleaning Up Drugs in Zhejiang Province should be in the excluded list and can still be strictly investigated and banned according to the province's separate regulations to eliminate the opium disaster. Please, Your Excellency, quickly wire the Central Government to approve the extension of the Provisional Regulations for Cleaning Up Drugs in Zhejiang Province for two years, so that it can continue to be strictly implemented to eliminate the opium disaster. The people of Zhejiang are very worried. The All Shanghai Zhejiang Provincial Association bows respectfully."

The Chinese Jisheng Association and other charities, such as the Huayang Yizhen Association, are handling spring relief in Yixing and Liyang. They are currently dispatching relief workers to conduct surveys by region. Relief in Yi includes investigating the four districts of 4, 5, 6, and 7. Relief in Li includes investigating the four districts of 1, 2, 3, and 6. Because the disaster areas in these two counties are very large and the resources of the charities are limited, they can only handle relief by region according to their capabilities. It has now been reported by the relief chief, Mr. Li Yunmen, that the relief in Yixing has completed the surveys of districts 6 and 7. There are more than 9,000 households in district 7 and 7,800 households in district 6. The number of households in other districts is also not small. The relief workers have personally witnessed that the disaster victims in the area either eat grass roots and tree bark, or eat Guanyin powder, appearing emaciated and barely alive. Some commit suicide by poisoning, drowning, or hanging. Others sell their children, resulting in separation or death. Others flee famine and never return, resulting in death and family destruction. Still others flee to other counties but are blocked from advancing and return to their hometowns, unable to survive and left to die. All kinds of tragic scenes are heartbreaking and bring tears to the eyes. If we calculate 5 or 6 family members per household, one district already has more than 9,000 households. The porridge is scarce, and there are too many monks, making it difficult to distribute. If one district is like this, other districts can be imagined. Even if the charity tries its best to solicit funds, its ability does not match its intentions. How much can it get? Moreover, because of rural bankruptcy and economic depression, fundraising has become difficult for charitable organizations. In this day and age, where can we find so much money to save the starving and rescue lives? We hope that charitable comrades within the country, while still alive, can offer ten spoons of soup to save a life, and share their clothes and food to create immeasurable blessings. This is the time to do so! By saving people today, they will surely receive good karma in the future. The disaster victims in the dried-up ruts are looking forward to it and waiting for orders.

Plant Pest and Disease Inspection to Begin Today; Fruits and Vegetables Imported and Exported via Shanghai Must Pass Inspection Before Customs Clearance 151

The plant pest and disease inspection drafted by the Ministry of Industry has now been decided to be implemented first in Shanghai, starting today (the 20th) by the Bureau of Commercial Inspection. The details are as follows:

Letter to the Chamber of Commerce: The Shanghai Bureau of Commercial Inspection sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, stating: "Based on the Ministry of Industry's Instruction No. 29781, we are copying and distributing the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of Plant Pest and Disease Inspection and the Table of Fruit and Vegetable Categories Subject to Inspection, and the Table of Inspection Fees. We are instructed to implement them first in Shanghai, etc. Therefore, this Bureau has decided to implement them in accordance with the order starting on the 20th of this month. In addition to publishing a public announcement, we are sending you the relevant Chinese and English Detailed Rules for the Implementation of Inspection and the Tables of Categories and Fees, 30 copies each, for your Chamber to forward to relevant industries for their information. From now on, fruit and vegetables imported and exported via Shanghai that are listed in the tables must be reported to this Bureau for inspection in accordance with the regulations and must pass inspection before being allowed to be imported or exported. Please investigate and handle the matter accordingly."

Inspection Categories: (1) Imported: (A) Fruits: Citrus, lemon, pomelo, citron, Buddha's hand, apple, quince, grape, pineapple, apricot, plum, banana, olive, papaya, jujube, persimmon, carambola, coconut, peach, fig, pear, cherry, pomegranate, walnut, chestnut, loquat, currant, gooseberry, pecan, mango, avocado, sugarapple, guava, cashew, imbu, redmonbin, yellowmonbin, chermoya, breadfruit, granadilla, and other various fruits. (B) Vegetables: Radish, turnip, carrot, rutabaga, yam, potato, sweet potato, beet, taro, lotus root, arrowhead, scallion, chives, shallot, ciboule, onion, garlic, asparagus, bamboo shoots, water chestnut, water shield, green vegetables, mustard greens, spinach, cabbage, lettuce, garland chrysanthemum, water spinach, artichoke, watermelon, loofah, eggplant, pepper, tomato, strawberry, lily, Jerusalem artichoke, endive, chicory, salsify, and other various vegetables. (2) Exported: (A) Fruits: Tangerine, pomelo, citron, Buddha's hand, lychee, longan, almond, chestnut, walnut, carambola, pear, pomegranate, plum, date, and other various fruits. (B) Vegetables: Turnip, potato, ginger, onion, asparagus, lily, and other various vegetables.

Inspection Fees: (A) Fruits: (1) Citrus, lemon, mango, longan, lychee, almond: 1 jiao (national currency) per dan (city system). (2) Apple, chestnut, walnut, grape, pecan, fig, banana, pomelo, coconut, olive, pineapple, red date, black date: 5 fen (national currency) per dan (city system). (3) Peach, pear, loquat, plum, apricot, carambola, persimmon, plum, pomegranate: 3 fen (national currency) per dan (city system). (4) Other fruits: 2 fen (national currency) per dan (city system). (B) Vegetables: 1 fen (national currency) per dan (city system). For all categories A and B above, if the reported goods are less than one dan (city system), they will be counted as one dan.

Township Residents in Luodian Town Are Superstitious; Offering Heavenly Provisions Causes Tragedy; More Than Thirty People Injured and Killed 154

Luodian Town in Baoshan County is the leading town at the border between the county and Jiading County. Its market is not inferior to Liuhe Town in Taicang County. There is a Jade Emperor Temple on North Street in the town, which is revered by the townspeople as the Heavenly Palace. Therefore, every year, the City God Temples in the surrounding villages must make offerings of heavenly provisions. In recent years, due to the impact of agricultural bankruptcy, the residents have become increasingly superstitious, believing that the heavenly provisions are insufficient and suspecting that the gods are causing trouble. Some people have long proposed making offerings of heavenly provisions. After Long County Chief heard about this, he issued a notice prohibiting it. Until yesterday afternoon at around 2:00 PM, the City God Temples in the four villages around the town, numbering as many as thirty-six, along with other secret inspectors' land temples, all carried paper-pasted silver ingots, etc., to the Jade Emperor Palace to offer provisions. Thousands of villagers from the four villages came to watch the excitement, causing the road to become congested. While the audience was absorbed in the spectacle, the stone railings on both sides of the Xin Bridge (behind the bus station) in the town suddenly collapsed with a loud crash. The audience on the bridge, along with the stones, all fell into the river. At that time, an old woman, aged sixty, whose son's name was Zhou Xunhe, lived in Zhoujia Village, southwest of Luodian. Her skull cracked and she died instantly. About thirty others were slightly or seriously injured. The villagers carried them back on their own, and their life or death cannot be investigated (some were as far as twenty li away). The rest were sent to the injured. The injured were bandaged by Doctor Li and others, and sent out. The seriously injured were all. The following is what was learned from yesterday's investigation: Fang Shenshi, 40 years old; Chen Shi, 40 years old; Hong Chenshi, 64 years old; Zhou Tushi, 70 years old; Jin Yangshi, 65 years old; Zhu Aizhong, 27 years old; Wang Yaoshi, 25 years old, all female. There were also males Liu Huisheng, 48 years old, and Shen Ayu, 20 years old, etc. All are currently not out of danger.

Parricide by Strangulation Case: Exhumation for Autopsy Held Yesterday; Yu Guanhong Addicted to Drugs and Fallen; Rope Marks Found on Neck 155

No. 2 New House, Yujiatang, south of Hongqiao Town, West Shanghai, is the address of Yu Huogen (62 years old), a local resident who makes a living by farming. He had a son named Guanhong (also known as Jilin), who is now 36 years old. He married a Chen and has one son and two daughters. Unfortunately, Guanhong does not engage in proper work, is greedy and lazy, and has addictions. Recently, he has been using morphine and smoking red pills. His father and wife have repeatedly advised him to quit, but to no avail. Therefore, his father hates him to the core. Starting this spring, Guanhong has been deprived of food. Guanhong has no choice but to go out to beg for food every day, looking like a beggar. Yu Huogen is extremely resentful of his unfilial son and has murderous intentions. Therefore, on the night of the 11th of this month, he colluded with his daughter-in-law, Chen (Guanhong's wife), and an accomplice, Zhang Ajin, and strangled Guanhong with a rope. The next day, they falsely claimed that he had died of illness and hastily put him in a coffin and buried him. However, rumors spread among the villagers, and they all said that Chen had murdered her husband. Now, the Hongqiao Town Police Station has learned of the situation. Because the case involves a human life, Yu Huogen and Yu Chen were summoned for interrogation the day before yesterday. After interrogation, Yu Huogen was released on bail, pending further instructions. At the same time, the police were ordered to escort Yu Chen to the local court. After questioning by Prosecutor Lei Binzhang, she was ordered to be detained pending further investigation. It was ordered to exhume the body for autopsy to clarify the truth. Yesterday afternoon, Prosecutor Lei, along with Examiner Xuan Zhiming, took a car to the countryside and went directly to Yujiatang, south of Hongqiao Town. The mortuary had already prepared everything, and the coffin of Yu Guanhong was carried to the mortuary. The small coffin workers opened the coffin and performed the autopsy according to the law. It was confirmed that the deceased Yu Guanhong had obvious rope marks on his neck, indicating that he had been strangled to death before his death. The death certificate was filled out, and it was ordered to reseal the coffin. After the judge completed the autopsy, Yu Huogen, the deceased's father, was summoned to the case for a brief interrogation. He was ordered to be handed over to the local bailiff for proper custody, pending further investigation. According to general accounts, Yu Huogen, in his twilight years, took advantage of his son's sound sleep and tightly strangled Guanhong's neck with a rope. Guanhong woke up from his sleep and resisted, and Yu Huogen called his daughter-in-law, Chen, to help him commit the crime. The deceased was no match and was eventually strangled to death.

Giant Snake Discovered in Ye Tomb in Pudong; Raising Head Towards Foreman; Grave Diggers Intended to Steal and Sell 156

Near the Milk Shed on Xujiaqiang, Yangjiadu, Pudong, a new road is being built. Beside it is a Ye family tomb field, covering an area of more than four mu. The grain deed holder is Ye Deru Tang. Many coffins are buried inside. The tomb field has been cultivated by gravekeeper Lu Heshang (over 70 years old). The Hua family descendants have not visited for more than ten years. Initially, the farmers rotated grain for cultivation. After it was developed into a road, the land prices on both sides rose sharply, and someone intercepted the grain deeds, stole the grain, and intended to steal and sell the land. Early in the morning the day before yesterday, a person resembling a foreman led more than twenty Jiangbei laborers, carrying tools, to excavate tombs in the tomb field. Twenty-six coffins were exhumed (more than ten of which had tombstones with the names, ages, and titles of the deceased, buried more than two hundred years ago). When one tomb was opened, poisonous snakes (red-banded snakes and gray snakes) were found. Many were several feet long to one or two zhang long, all of which were killed by the laborers with iron tools. Among them was a giant snake of more than five zhang long, with a head the size of a large bowl, blood-red all over, and eyes like blood. The foreman ordered the workers to beat and tie it according to law. The giant snake seemed to be spiritual, and upon hearing this, it raised its head towards the foreman, acting as if it were begging for mercy. The ignorant workers shouted that it was kowtowing and begging for mercy. The foreman then ordered the workers to stop beating and tying it, and let it go. The giant snake then swam to the edge of the field and turned its head back towards the foreman. At that time, many nearby villagers heard the news and went to watch. Later, they saw the giant snake swimming towards a certain family's tomb field nearby. The laborers removed the corpses from the exhumed coffins and placed them in bone boxes (shaped like soap boxes) for relocation elsewhere. When the tombs were being dug, the gravekeeper Lu Heshang and the foreman of the diggers had a dispute over the unearthed tombstones. Lu managed to seize six tombstones. He has now found the descendants of the tomb owner and is seriously negotiating with the grave diggers. It is reported that the tomb field has been exchanged by the grave diggers for a land business license from the Land Bureau, and the grain has been transferred in preparation for stealing and selling the land.

Small Vendors Selling Poisonous Candy – Many Children Die from Poisoning – Parents Should Pay Close Attention 157

A candy vendor came to Yangxing Village, northwest of Wusong, a few days ago, selling yellow sugar blocks at a very low price. For only two or three copper coins, one could buy a foot-square piece of sugar, or exchange it for old copper and scrap iron. However, they would not exchange it for rags or old clothes. This sugar seemed to be made of dry flour mixed with saccharin and soda, so it fermented very strongly. Children in the area, because of its low price, competed to buy and eat it. Unexpectedly, those who consumed it suffered from poisoning, abdominal distension, and severe pain. Before they could be rescued, six children, including those with the surname Li, died from eating this sugar. After the incident, the vendor had already fled without a trace. Upon learning of the situation, the Baoshan County Public Security Bureau immediately dispatched police to search for him everywhere. They have already captured several other candy vendors and are conducting a strict investigation. It is also reported that similar incidents have occurred in the villages near the Wusong Fort in Taiwan. Therefore, recently, schools and parents in the Wusong area have warned all students and children not to buy candy from vendors again to avoid endangering their lives. It is said that the toxic effects of this poisonous candy are not immediately apparent after consumption, and illness only occurs after several days. Taking lily root and reed rhizome, etc., can supposedly detoxify, but it is not known for sure. It is deeply hoped that the health authorities will take appropriate measures to handle the aftermath.

Foreman Shot by Bandits at Midnight – Bandits with Painted Faces 158

Tang Fusheng, a native of Tongzhou, resides at No. 4, Lane 120, Yangjiazhai, Pudong. He works as a foreman in the cold working section of the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Lujiazui. At 11 o'clock the night before last, Tang was sound asleep when he suddenly heard urgent knocking on the door and his name being called repeatedly. Tang woke up with a start, got up, pulled the bolt, and opened the door. Suddenly, two men with painted faces and wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers pointed handguns at Tang's face and fired. The bullet entered through Tang's nose and became deeply embedded. Tang was injured, collapsed to the ground, and lost consciousness. Seeing that their purpose had been achieved, the assailants fled without a trace. Tang's wife immediately reported the incident to the Pudong Sub-bureau. Captain Wang of the bureau's detective team led officers to arrest the assailants. Two bullets were found at the entrance of the house, but the assailants were nowhere to be found. The injured Tang was carried by his family to Pudong Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he was transferred to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. Director Zhang of the sub-bureau yesterday instructed detectives to rigorously pursue and apprehend the criminals to bring them to justice.

Zhou Fashan's Sudden Death Case – Male and Female Ruffians Use Pretexts to Extort Money – Involvement of Detectives Using Torture to Extract Confessions – Corpse's Wife Voluntarily Opens Coffin for Re-examination 159

Zhou Fashan, a native of Liuhe County, and Xu Zhenggui, a native of Nanjing, both earned their living by selling straw in the Hongkou area. Zhou's sister-in-law, Lin, ran a stove shop at No. 1 Miller Road, so Zhou lodged at his sister-in-law's house, while Xu rented a garret at No. 142 Jiaxing Road. They became friends in their poverty. On the morning of the 28th of last month, Zhou and Xu went together to the Pinfang Teahouse next to the Jiaxing Road Police Station to drink tea and chat. Suddenly, Wang Agui, a follower of the local ruffian Xu Songbao, and his mistress, Ama, led more than a dozen people and swarmed upstairs. Wang immediately accused Zhou of introducing Ama to someone for adultery and receiving a reward of thirty yuan, ordering him to hand over the money. Both Zhou and Xu firmly denied it. Wang then, seeing that both men were paupers, reduced the amount to fifteen yuan. However, Zhou and Xu still claimed ignorance and, feeling intimidated by the crowd, went downstairs to avoid them. Just as they stepped out of the teahouse, they were intercepted by Jin Awu, an informant, and Zhang Desheng, a detective from the Jiaxing Road Police Station, and taken into the police station. After questioning by the head detective, Xu was released, while Zhou Fashan suddenly suffered an acute illness and died before he could receive medical treatment. The head detective ordered the body to be sent to the coroner's office. On the 30th, a report was made to the First Special District Local Court, and a prosecutor was appointed to lead a forensic doctor to the office.

Upon examination, the forensic doctor determined that the deceased had no injuries on his body and that he had died from a sudden heart attack due to stress. However, at that time, the deceased's wife, Zhou Zhao, was still in her hometown of Liuhe. Zhou Lin, the sister-in-law of the deceased, went to the station and refused to acknowledge that her uncle had died of illness, refusing to sign and claim the body. The prosecutor then ordered Pushan Villa to provide a coffin and temporarily bury the body. Later, the deceased's wife, Zhou Zhao, received a telegram and came to Shanghai, hiring a lawyer along with Xu Zhenggui to file a

criminal lawsuit against Jin Awu, Zhang Desheng, Wang Agui, and Ama and others in the First Special District Local Court, accusing Wang and his mistress Ama of using pretexts to extort money, and Jin and Zhang of using torture to extract confessions, resulting in injury and death, requesting that they be punished according to the law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan held a court hearing, but all four defendants failed to appear. Only the two plaintiffs, Zhou Zhao and Xu Zhenggui, and the witness Zhou Lin, came forward. The court first questioned Xu Zhenggui, who testified that at around 11 o'clock that morning, he and Zhou Fashan were drinking tea at Pinfang Teahouse when Wang Agui and Ama led more than a dozen people upstairs and attempted to extort money under false pretenses. They ignored them and immediately went downstairs, but were detained by Jin Awu and Zhang Desheng and taken to the police station. A foreigner first questioned Zhou

briefly. Because Zhou denied soliciting prostitution on behalf of others, Jin took Zhou away, and he never saw Zhou again. Later, he was also taken by Jin to another room for questioning and was slapped on both cheeks with a shoe sole. He is now also accusing Jin and Zhang of using torture to extract confessions, and accusing Wang et al. of attempted extortion. As for how Zhou died and whether he bled at the police station, he could not know because he did not see him. However, he heard Jin Awu say that Zhou was ill, and then said that Zhou had died of illness, but he knew that Zhou

had no signs of illness, etc. Then Zhou Zhao testified that she came to Shanghai after receiving a telegram from her hometown and was informed of everything by Xu Zhenggui before filing the lawsuit, etc. The plaintiff's lawyer then asked the court to examine the evidence of Zhou Zhao's accusation of torture to extract confessions in order to facilitate the investigation. He then requested on behalf of the woman to re-open the coffin and examine the body, saying that the evidence regarding torture to extract confessions was particularly difficult to collect. In order to accurately clarify the cause of death, it would be best to ask the Zhenru Forensic Institute to re-examine the body. The woman then expressed her willingness to open the coffin for re-examination. Judge Wu then adjourned the hearing until a later date.

Xiang Huian Invents High-Speed Magnesium Flash Camera 160

Xiang Huian, a member of the China Black and White Photography Society, has a deep understanding of photography. Since becoming the chief photographer of the International News Photography Agency, he has been particularly interested in news photography. He felt that the old methods of magnesium flash photography were inconvenient and that it was impossible to photograph indoor and outdoor night sports photos, which he considered a pity. He resolved to research and overcome all the difficulties of high-speed photography in dark places. Recently, he assembled a high-speed magnesium flash camera that can take photographs of moving objects in indoor and outdoor dark places at speeds of 1/10th to 1/1000th of a second. It is easy to carry and simple to use. He has conducted several tests, all of which have been satisfactory. He is currently continuing to research and develop a high-speed magnesium flash lamp vapor camera, which will be completed soon.

Spring Fishing Season Production and Sales Decline – Authorities Pay Attention to Fishermen's Suffering – Vigorously Promote Cooperative Enterprises 169

According to the Central News Agency, many fishermen live along the coast of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces in China, and fish production is very high. However, due to the dumping of foreign goods and rampant piracy, and the fact that fishermen's fishing techniques are mostly outdated, the fishing industry has not been revitalized. This year, it has been further affected by the recession, which has had a major impact on the fishing industry. The authorities are now trying to rescue the situation. The details are as follows:

Falling Fish Prices: Since the spring fishing season this year, due to unfavorable weather and cold temperatures, although fishermen have tried their best to fish, their catches have been much lower than last year. Moreover, due to the impact of the recession, people's purchasing power is very weak, so sales are sluggish and prices have to fall. Last year, yellow croaker reached 9 yuan per dan, but this year it is only about 3 yuan. Fishermen originally regarded the spring fishing season as a period of mass production, but this year the catch is small and the price is low, which will have a major impact on the livelihoods of fishermen.

Authorities Pay Attention: The authorities are now paying close attention to the suffering of fishermen. Regarding the prevention of bandits, strict measures have been taken in recent years, so there has been no trace of bandits this year. Regarding production and sales, they are vigorously promoting cooperative enterprises and guiding the improvement of fishing methods. It is not appropriate for the current fishermen to stick to outdated methods. In the future, they will gradually plan to use fishing vessels for large-scale fishing. Regarding the required funding, the authorities are trying their best to find ways.

Building Fishing Ports: The authorities are also paying close attention to the construction of fishing ports. They have sent personnel to inspect the ports in various fishing areas in order to start building fishing ports in the future. However, the construction of fishing ports requires a lot of money, which is difficult to realize at a time when the national treasury is stretched. Moreover, the construction of fishing ports is not necessary at present. China still lacks large-scale fishing methods. In the future, fishing methods can be improved, and the production of fish can be increased by using large fishing vessels. Then fishing ports must be built. Therefore, it is only in the planning stage at present.

Zhang Shouyong Discusses Real Estate Investment Issues – Says New Village Real Estate Investment Methods are Sound – Shanghai People Should Shift Their Focus to the Suburbs 174

Recently, newspapers have published suggestions from the China New Village Construction Society on reforming the real estate investment system, advocating a new village real estate cooperative investment method to break the market deadlock. The reporter then visited Mr. Zhang Shouyong, a member of the Fund Management Committee of the China Economic Credit Cooperative, which manages the investment funds of the society, to ask for his opinion. According to him, he knows the new method in great detail. The society's new village real estate cooperative investment is partly to expand the scope of the Qiangwei Garden New Village and partly to open up a new path for real estate investors. The method was devised by specialized talent who devoted themselves to research and sought advice from economists, so it is

quite sound. For example, (1) investors are not limited by financial resources, (2) the drawbacks of vacant rentals are avoided, (3) the interest rate on real estate investment is increased, (4) management, repair, and depreciation expenses are reduced, (5) all real estate is individually guaranteed and the original value is reduced by 10%, and (6) there is no difficulty in selling ordinary real estate, etc. These are all its advantages. In the current state of economic downturn, this is the only stable path for real estate investors. At present, there are many shortcomings in the real estate industry. If the new village real estate cooperative investment method is used as a blueprint to thoroughly reform the real estate investment system, then the future of the real estate industry may be promising. In my opinion, the greatest significance of new village real estate cooperative investment lies in encouraging

rural investment and promoting rural construction. In recent years, the bankruptcy of rural areas in the interior has also affected the crisis in Shanghai's future. Now, people have realized the current crisis, and everyone has attempted to go to the interior. For example, the number of banks going to the interior to establish branches has gradually increased. However, general real estate investors still regard this path as a dangerous one because interior investment lacks protection. Investors should be concerned about the issue of whether lending to the interior is appropriate. However, I believe that the beginning of all undertakings must have a great spirit. On the other hand, we must plan a good way to deal with the environment. Now, the society is opening up a stable path for those who want to invest in rural areas, and everyone does not have to doubt whether lending to the interior is appropriate. I hope that Shanghai people will shift their focus to the interior, open up their own prosperous gardens, and promote Shanghai's development.

Health Bureau to Start Vaccinations on May 1 – Compulsory Vaccinations for Slum Dwellers – Schools and Factories to Proceed in Order 175

The Shanghai Health Bureau is concerned about the spread of epidemics and the detriment to hygiene as summer approaches, so its epidemic prevention work brooks no delay. According to Yu Jihua, director of the Hunnan Health Clinic, the bureau has decided to start vaccinations in various places from May 1. The issue of funding has been submitted to the municipal government for allocation, and they are now actively preparing medicines, materials, and equipment for application. The details are as follows:

Additional Personnel: Vaccinations in Groups

The Health Bureau will routinely add more than a dozen temporary personnel in the summer to specialize in epidemic prevention work, from May 1 to September 15, which can be completed in about four and a half months. Three groups of six people will be set up to carry the medicines to start work first. Eight more vaccination groups will be added in June to prevent infection.

Compulsory Vaccination for Slum Dwellers

According to the situation in previous years, epidemics mostly occur in slums, the reason being unhygienic diet and living. Therefore, cholera, typhoid, and bacillary dysentery are the most common diseases in summer and are extremely contagious. Therefore, it has been decided this year that it is necessary to force vaccinations on every household in the slums.

Schools and Factories: Vaccinations in Order

Prior notice will be sent to all public and private primary and secondary schools in the city to arrange dates and times. Personnel will be sent to the schools during the summer vacation to provide vaccinations in order to prevent the spread of epidemics. As for the male and female workers in the various factories in the city, they will also be notified in advance in accordance with the above-mentioned method and dates will be set before personnel are sent to administer vaccinations.

Budgeted Expenses: Approximately 30,000 Yuan

The bureau's vaccinations, regardless of age, require at least two injections per person, preferably three. The budget for staff salaries, transportation, meals, and equipment, medicines, materials, and other expenses, calculated at 80,000 injections, requires approximately 30,000 yuan. Director Li has submitted a request to the municipal government for allocation.

Pregnant Woman Dies Tragically After Abortion; Lover and Midwife Sentenced 176

A woman surnamed Wang, known as Wang Bao, from the northern countryside of Yangzhou, was 28 years old this year. She had a husband and three children at home, earning a living by farming. Due to famine in her hometown, she came to Shanghai alone to work as a domestic helper to earn wages and supplement the family income. She worked for a family surnamed Mou in Yuqing Lane, Wenzhou Road. Last November, while fetching water, she met Li Xiujian, a fellow villager who worked as a back scrubber at the Hot Springs Bathhouse on Rue Doumer. This year, he is 24 years old. The two immediately took a liking to each other and engaged in a clandestine affair. After several encounters, she became pregnant. Fearing she would lose face in front of her husband if she gave birth, she discussed the matter with her lover. They decided to have an abortion. On the 28th of last month, she was accompanied by Fu Pei to the home of Li Wang, an elderly midwife from Nanjing (68 years old this year), located at No. 6, Rue Pottier in the French Concession, to request an abortion. They agreed on a price of fifteen yuan, which was paid. Wang then stayed at the midwife's home. The next day, the midwife gave her a root of medicinal herb and a dose of labor-inducing drugs. On the afternoon of the 30th, the fetus was aborted. On the 1st of this month, Li Xiujian went to pick her up. However, due to internal injuries, she suffered unbearable abdominal pain. On the morning of the 3rd, Li took her to Huilü Hospital on Avenue Haig. He falsely claimed that she had a miscarriage and sought treatment. However, the treatment was ineffective, and she died on the morning of the 4th. After examining her condition, the doctor determined that it was definitely not a miscarriage but was caused by a forced abortion. He reported it to the Xinzha Police Station, who sent detectives to arrest Li Xiujian and take him to the police station. The French police station dispatched Detective Bu Zhenglong to arrest the midwife, Li Wang, and sent the body to the coroner's office. The Second Special District Court sent personnel to investigate and confirm the cause of death. Since no family members of the deceased could be found, the body was buried by a charity organization. Meanwhile, the Chinese police station sent Li Wang and Li Xiujian to the Second Special District Court. The prosecutor, based on articles 306 and 308 of the Criminal Code regarding the crime of abortion, filed a public prosecution. These details have already been reported in the newspapers. Presiding Judge Sun Peng interrogated and concluded the case. Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., Judge Sun presided over the criminal court and ordered the defendants to be brought to court. Li Wang was sentenced to two years and four months of imprisonment for performing an abortion at the request of a pregnant woman, resulting in the woman's death. Li Xiujian was sentenced to two years and three months of imprisonment for instigating an abortion resulting in the woman's death. The number of days detained before the final judgment was determined, with two days of detention offsetting two days of imprisonment. Within the appeal period, both defendants will be held in the detention center pending further instructions.

Girl Dies of Hemophilia; Unrelated to Midwife's Treatment 177

Lu Fubao, a local resident, 26 years old, working as a member of the security corps in the Chinese district, lives at No. 156, Zhongzhou Road, Zhabei. He recently had a daughter named Xuezhen, just over a month old. A white growth suddenly appeared on the child's gums, commonly known as "mantis eggs." Lu hired Ma Pan, a kind person and a midwife living at No. 622, Chen Da Lane, Ju Tong Road, to treat the child. The condition did not improve, and after being sent to the hospital, she died. The Hongkou Police Station, upon receiving the report, ordered detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the coroner's office on Avenue Foch. The First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Guo Lian, along with a forensic doctor, to examine the body. Since the cause of death could not be determined from the external appearance, and fearing that the midwife's treatment was negligent and led to death, for the sake of caution, it was ordered that an autopsy be performed for a detailed examination. This was reported in this newspaper a few days ago. Yesterday morning, the forensic doctor of the First Special District Court completed the autopsy. It was found that the child died of hemophilia. The diagnosis by Ma Pan had no bearing on the death. Therefore, Prosecutor Guo and others went to the office to inform the relevant police station and the family of the deceased of the above situation. It was concluded that the deceased girl, Lu Xuezhen, died of hemophilia. The body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial.

Woman Loses Her Life Over Twenty Cents 178

Han Xuezhong, from Gaoyou, 21 years old, a dockworker, lives in a simple shed without a number at the southern end of Ao Jiazhai Road, Peidong. His wife, Yang, 23 years old, has a two-year-old son. The couple had a good relationship. On the 17th of this month, Han's brother-in-law visited for the first time and brought lucky money of eighty cents, distributing it to Han's son and the neighborhood children. At that time, Yang collected forty cents. In the evening, Han's mother thought that Yang should not keep all the money and wanted to get twenty cents back from her. Because of this, the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law started arguing. Unexpectedly, Han's mother became angry and grabbed Yang's hair, hitting her slightly. Yang was angry and cried in bed. When Han returned home from work, he also blamed her for disobeying his mother. Yang became even more angry. The next evening (the 18th), Han suddenly saw that Yang's body was slightly swollen and she was mentally unclear, as if she had taken poison. He hurriedly sent her to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. The hospital diagnosed that her condition was critical and could not be saved. She was carried back home and died at 8 a.m. At that time, Han and his mother both fled in fear. It was not until evening that a neighbor reported it to the Peidong Public Security Bureau. The bureau, considering the case involved a human life, immediately summoned the local leader, Zhang Dunlong. Yesterday morning at 9 a.m., Zhang requested the local court to send Prosecutor Kong to conduct an on-site examination. There were no injuries on the surface. To clarify the truth of the death, it was decided to have the body transported to the Zhenru Examination Institute today for an autopsy. The deceased's husband also surrendered to the Pudong branch yesterday to await questioning. According to nearby neighbors, the deceased seemed to have died from swallowing sulfur ore.

After Separating from His Concubine, Chen Dimin Has a Dispute with His Wife 179

Chen Dimin, a wealthy businessman currently living at No. 15, Lafayette New Village, Route Lafayette, in the French Concession, is 43 years old this year. He used to be a comprador for a foreign firm. He married Tan Kunfan from Wuxing (39 years old this year). They have been married for nearly 20 years and have six children, two sons and four daughters. The couple's relationship has always been very good. Ten years ago, Chen took Hu Luo'e, a prostitute from Suzhou (31 years old this year; her sister was once elected the first Flower Queen), as his concubine. They lived together in Dazhong Lane, Tongfu Road. However, two years ago, disagreements arose. Chen stopped visiting and ignored Hu. Hu was forced to file a petition with the Second Special District Court, requesting a support order. This was previously reported in the newspaper. After the trial, the court ordered Chen to pay her 1,000 yuan. Chen was not satisfied with the original judgment and is now appealing to the Third High Court. On February 27 of this year, Chen and his wife, Chen Tan Kunfan, suddenly had an argument over a trivial matter and began fighting. After family members intervened, Tan Kunfan angrily took her three or four daughters and left home to live with her mother. Relatives and friends repeatedly mediated and tried to persuade her to return, but Tan refused. Chen then hired lawyer Xu Yannian to file a petition with the Civil Mediation Office of the Second Special District Court, requesting mediation for reconciliation. Chen Tan Kunfan also hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Hua Maosheng. Yesterday, Judge Li Liang of the Second Special District Court opened the seventh civil court for mediation. The applicant was represented by a lawyer, who stated that both parties were unable to attend the hearing due to other important matters and requested that the mediation be postponed. The court verified the statement and approved the request, ordering that the mediation be rescheduled for the 23rd.

Report from the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Association on Sending Relief Workers to Liyang 180

The Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Association on Renji Road, due to the severe drought and spring famine in various places, has been working together with the Jisheng Association and other charitable organizations. However, both financial and human resources are severely insufficient. Liyang is in urgent need of relief. The association has specially transferred Mr. Yu, a relief worker stationed in Changzhou, to assist Mr. Li Yunmen, the director dispatched to the area, in investigating the situation. According to Mr. Yu's report, the association is responsible for relief in the first, second, third, and sixth districts of Liyang, together with the Jisheng Association. The first, third, and second districts are the most urgent. At this time of year, when the old crops have run out and the new crops have yet to come in, the disaster victims are mainly filling their stomachs with wild vegetables and Guanyin soil. Recently, they have exhausted everything they can dig up and are resorting to eating grass and tree bark. Entering their homes, the pungent smell of grass is unbearable. Many of those who fled to Wuxi and Changzhou have been sent back. Deaths from starvation occur in every village, and refugees are everywhere, a truly miserable sight. The situation in the first, second, third, and sixth districts is particularly urgent. If relief is delayed any longer, the consequences will be unthinkable. The best way to provide emergency relief is to distribute relief tickets. Sometimes, when people are about to die of starvation, giving them soybean cakes can immediately turn the situation around. Having witnessed the truth with his own eyes, he cannot remain silent. The association feels that both financial and human resources are lacking and urgently hopes that all sectors of society can provide assistance to save these remaining lives.

(1) Chen Zhengfa, from Ningbo, 20 years old, checked into room 14 of the Xiaohua Runhua Hotel on Zhejiang Road on the 12th of this month and showed no unusual behavior. A Lysol bottle was found next to the bed, indicating that he had taken poison. The police were notified, and he was sent to the hospital for treatment. His condition is very critical. (2) Yin Chuntong, from Zhenjiang, checked into the Shengtai Hotel on Tianjin Road on the 14th. He claimed to be 28 years old. The hotel assigned him room 20 for his stay. However, at about 7 a.m. yesterday, a tea boy from the hotel suddenly discovered that Yin had secretly swallowed sleeping pills in his room to commit suicide. The police were immediately notified, and he was taken to the hospital for treatment. Due to the overdose of poison, his life is in danger. (3) At about 8:30 p.m. yesterday, a bathhouse customer, about 40 years old, went to the Shuangfeng Pavilion Bathhouse at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Fujian Road to take a bath. Going to See Peonies: Nanjing Linggu Temple, Guojiadou in Punan, Songjiang 183

The peony is the king of flowers, but it is difficult to cultivate, and good varieties are extremely rare. In addition to the peonies at Chongxiao Temple in Beiping, which are famous (but still far from blooming), the peonies in Linggu Temple in Nanjing have many valuable varieties and are highly regarded. In addition, the Qin family courtyard in Guojiadou Village, Punan, Songjiang, has peony plants that were left over from the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty, more than 300 years ago. Despite repeated changes, only this plant remains. Its quality is extremely high, the flowers are as big as bowls, and the petals are deep red and purple, exquisite and brilliant, rare in the world. People with a fondness for peonies in Nanjing and other places often travel long distances to see them when they bloom. According to a person from the village, the peonies in Qin's collection already have seven or eight buds and are expected to bloom by the end of this month. It takes about four hours to hire a private boat from Songjiang to Yinyin, and a 45-minute walk from the shore to Guojiadou Village. The round-trip boat fare is about two yuan. During this beautiful spring season, there will be many people going to Linggu Temple and Guojiadou to see the flowers.

(2) Review and Expectations of the Publishing World (Continued) - Ye Qing

The Way Out for the Publishing World 199

— Fan Zhongyun

China's publishing industry has never had a publishing plan from the beginning, relying entirely on market needs to publish books on a case-by-case basis, which is similar to market speculation. This is because large bookstores have never thought of publishing books in a planned way, while small bookstores, although consciously wanting to have a plan, are limited by their financial resources and cannot do so. Moreover, most small bookstores take large bookstores as their standard, following their steps closely and imitating them without any hesitation. Therefore, China's new book industry, since the Commercial Press pioneered it, many subsequent companies have been similar to the Commercial Press, rarely specializing in one type of book and establishing their own unique style. Because of this, the competition between them in the market is extremely fierce. This can still be dealt with when the market is active, but when the market is sluggish, it becomes difficult to find books to publish.

Because books lack sales, the idea of a publishing plan came to mind, but this so-called plan, based on recent market performance, seems to be more of a lazy and inherited mindset than an active and creative tendency. For example, the reprinting of large collections of ancient books and the compilation of so-called libraries are mostly based on existing books, piecing them together. This is a makeshift solution, so if it is said that this is intended to open up a new situation, it would be better to say that it is maintaining the status quo in order to cope with this sluggish market, which is still equivalent to having no plan. However, even this kind of unplanned approach cannot be undertaken by large bookstores with considerable financial resources, let alone small bookstores.

For the present, if we want to create a new situation and contribute a corresponding effort to our own business and to the culture of the nation, then first, I believe that we must break the habit of following the crowd. When we see that a certain bookstore is publishing a book that sells well, everyone comes to publish that book. Second, each bookstore should be able to distinguish itself and specialize in a certain type of book. In general, the more specialized the division of labor in a production industry, the better the quality. I think the publishing industry should also be like this. Especially for small bookstores, which are limited in their ability, there is no need to model themselves after the Commercial Press, trying to do too much and gather everything together. In this way, competition between them can be eased, and there is the possibility of cooperation. Third, in today's developed production, as a rule, producers and distributors must divide labor, and there is no reason to produce and sell by oneself. Therefore, I believe that if small bookstores want to survive in this sluggish situation, it is necessary to jointly establish a common retail outlet in order to save expenses and concentrate management. Only in this way can we prevent the manipulation of intermediaries in other cities, which will benefit readers' purchases.

As for large publishers, I believe that with their strong financial resources, they do not need to compete with small bookstores, but should set their own publishing plans. To be honest, we now have all kinds of books in fragments, without systematic editing and printing. For example, in literature, do we have a literary history and works that include ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign? Therefore, introductions to the literary history of various countries and eras, as well as the works of various important writers, are the most needed at present. Not only in literature, but also in politics, economics, philosophy, science, etc., it is the same. In the vertical aspect, we need a systematic historical introduction, and in the horizontal aspect, we urgently need a clear understanding of different categories. This can only be done with the abilities of fire publishers.

Review and Expectations of the Publishing World (Continued) 200

— Ye Qing

We should not be fatalists, we should do and we should think of ways to correct. Fundamentally, we must seek production development. And how to obtain the possibility of production development, such as enabling tariffs to be completely autonomous in order to protect nascent production, is also a problem, and it cannot be solved in the short term. Does the publishing industry stop at this time to wait? Or continue to operate? I think it should operate. This is like workers who still have to live and have to do things to improve their current lives before a fundamental solution is found.

On the other hand, everything is done by people. If we do not understand our own shortcomings, we can continue to do it in the same old way. But once we understand, we should not only reform, but we also have the possibility to do so. There is room for free will here. We are not unconscious animals, we want to consciously practice and pursue the purpose we desire.

Here, I first feel that it is entirely possible to publish more philosophy and science books and fewer ancient books. The only question is whether the people in charge of various aspects of the publishing industry, such as the editors-in-chief of bookstores, understand the pros and cons of this. Regarding this point, I would like to discuss it in another article. Here, I treat the problem as if it has been solved. From now on, we will publish more philosophy, science books, and even literature books.

Of course, there are fewer buyers for advanced works. But I think it will increase. In any case, education and production are developing, albeit slowly. There is also some progress in research facilities and efforts. Although these are not enough, they can always add a bit of purchasing power. On the other hand, fewer ancient books will shift the purchasing power of ancient books to this aspect. Therefore, advanced works also have considerable sales.

Regarding the matter of publishing more philosophy, science books, and their advanced works, I believe that publishing entrepreneurs cannot completely stand in a passive position and only seek to supply objective needs. We must understand that publishing entrepreneurs are the conditions for creating the objective needs of researchers. Without new-style novels, people can only read old-style novels. With new-style novels, people will buy them and read them. Need arises from existence. The need to take the train comes from the existence of the train.

As for the problem of increasing quantity, it is related to funding. If the sales and production of the above-mentioned books are not commensurate, money is also needed to turn around. What to do? I think publishing entrepreneurs in all aspects should unite to demand subsidies. Since culture is important, and construction and revival are to be sought, publishing subsidies can be included in the legitimate expenditures of the state. Rather than spending money to support redundant agencies, it is better to abolish some and transfer people to translation and writing, and transfer money to publishing subsidies to be converted into royalties or royalties to pay them. There is still meaning.

To develop culture, it is necessary to develop the publishing industry. Therefore, after reviewing the publishing industry, I put forward my expectations. I hope that those engaged in publishing and culture will pay attention.

Casual Talks on Everyday Psychology 201

— Zu Shun

Dr. Jeeph Jastrow Translated by Zeng Baochi

Life Bookstore Price: One Yuan

Every year, when a new class of students comes into the classroom, I always give them a test—regarding their general state of mind. What surprises me is that among these college students in their prime, so many are pessimistic; they feel hopeless about their future, and there are many things in society that make them helpless—afraid, and feel the pain of the contradiction between thought and life. Several people even deeply feel their shortcomings and sincerely discuss rescue methods with me. Although I have also read a few psychology books, I cannot think of any principles or rules that can help them.

When I saw the book "Casual Talks on Everyday Psychology," I flipped through its table of contents, which seemed to be very related to several questions I often thought about in my heart. However, after reading it in detail, I was disappointed. It was not because it did not answer my questions. Originally, this end-of-the-century disease cannot be cured not only by this young psychology, but even philosophy, although it is more effective than psychology, is not a good prescription for removing the root of the disease. These sad youth, unless they understand that they should be doctors themselves to help people—after discovering the real root of the disease—they will not be saved. Psychology is powerless, and at the same time, it is certainly not to blame this book.

My disappointment with this book is that what it says is too limited to "psychology." The author absolutely does not separate the influence of social organization on individual psychology, so that what is achieved is very limited. Although it is such a thick book, I still want to introduce this book to people who want to know what psychology is and who are deterred by the nerve organization, stimuli, and reactions in psychology textbooks. Here, the author talks about everyday life in a plain and unremarkable way, without talking about any laws or proposing any rules, but after you read it, in many aspects, you can indeed understand yourself and people's behavior "psychologically." You will know how a small action or habit hides a very serious or very interesting meaning.

Throughout the book, the author mostly analyzes without giving answers. Occasionally, his sermons are not very sound and are too submissive to the social status quo. For example, the Professor Bokham children's mental health rules he cites say that children should be made to believe in religion and revere the master of heaven and earth: and when explaining that cousins can marry, he cites the story of Sarah and Abraham in the Old Testament as one of the bases, which is simply as ridiculous as Kang Liang citing "Three years without changing the way of the father, it can be called filial piety" to advocate that the ancestral laws can be modified.

There are several sections in this book that can be specially introduced, such as the following sections. In the first chapter; section 10, how to fill the deficiencies in your soul; section 12, the tragedy caused by fixation; section 18, stubbornness; in the second chapter; section 10, fatigue is a dangerous symbol for children; section 16, should it be beaten or should it not be beaten; section 17, degenerate; in the third chapter; section 3, why do you want to act; section 6, do you hate people; in the fourth chapter; section 7, the relationship between mood and work: in the sixth chapter, the ingenuity of makeup; in the tenth chapter: section 11, the subconscious and habits, etc. These sections are all written well, but I always feel that they could be written better.

Regarding the translation, the second half seems to be better than the first half. There are several terms that can be discussed, such as translating Forgetting as amnesia.

Introduction to Bacon's "New Organon" (Continued) 202

— Du Ruoyi

Published by Xin Ken Bookstore Translated by Shen Yinming

"New Organon" is Bacon's masterpiece. Even his most critical critics cannot but say: "Bacon's greatest work is the first volume of "New Organon"" (Macaulay). Before Bacon, the only method of studying science was Aristotle's logic—that is, syllogism. In this book, Bacon advocated a new logic, namely induction, which was completed by John Stuart Mill. It is a major feature of modern research methods, which was not available in medieval research methods. Bacon's original plan was to attempt a comprehensive work called "The Great Instauration", divided into six parts: the first part was an overview of the intellectual state at the time; the second part discussed how to correctly use the intellect when explaining nature; the third part reclassified the various phenomena of the universe as materials applicable to the new method; the fourth part explained the application of the new method and its results; the fifth part narrated the facts achieved by the author in natural philosophy using his original method; and the sixth part was the prediction of the results of applying the new philosophy, that is, the new method, to all phenomena in the universe. However, most of this plan was never completed. Only the first part became "The Advancement of Learning" and the second part became "New Organon" and was realized. The others were all fragments, and the sixth part was never written at all. Therefore, the book "New Organon" is only a part of "The Great Instauration", and even the book itself was not completed. According to the author in section 21 of the second volume of this book, the problems to be discussed in this book are: (1) specially selected examples: (2) inductive supports: (3) inductive revisions; (4) research methods vary according to the nature of the topic; (5) the nature of specially selected examples: (6) the scope of research; (7) application; (8) preparation for research: (9) the stages of axiomatic decline, etc., but only one specially selected example is actually discussed in this book: other items are not only not mentioned in this book, but also not found in other works.

This book is written in Latin. The content is divided into two parts: the first part refutes Aristotle's style of argumentation and points out the shortcomings of various previous theories. This can be said to be "intellectual cleansing", which is "breaking evil". In the second part, he put forward his new logic, which is "manifesting the correct". Therefore, the defect of this book lies in the second part, but the first part also has many points of interest, such as explaining the arrival of a new era in science and the theory of idols, etc.

Bacon has an immortal slogan: "Knowledge is power". His entire thought is an expansion and completion of this concept. Bacon realized that all the knowledge that humans have always possessed is useless. But he believed that knowledge could originally become a power. He saw that the existing knowledge in the world—especially the knowledge about nature—had no results and was not reliable. With this kind of knowledge, humans cannot control nature. Therefore, he felt hopeless about the previous sciences. But he believed that if humans could use new methods, the highest power to control nature could be restored. However, to use new methods, it is necessary to completely abandon the medieval doctrines and rules. People must be like infants, not infected by any doctrines or ideas, cleanse all prejudices and reduce the idols (Idols) in their hearts.

The idol that Bacon said refers to a false image being regarded as an entity, and an idea being regarded as a physical object. He believed that idols are the source of all fallacies, and the types of idols can be divided into four, namely "idols of the tribe", "idols of the cave", "idols of the market", and "idols of the theater".

Bacon's theory has had a very great impact on European culture. His era was just after the dark ages of the Middle Ages. European knowledge increased, and terror decreased; people worshiped "unknowable" thoughts less, and I won more unknowable thoughts. All the spirits of life were inspired by a new belief; obstacles were overthrown. This was an era of success, hope, and vitality; an era of new beginnings and new undertakings in all fields: this era was waiting for a call, and needed a comprehensive mind to summarize its spirit and judgment. This was Bacon. 、

In short, Bacon is the most powerful mind in modern times. His theory is very important. Now, his masterpiece "New Organon" has been translated into Chinese by Mr. Shen Yinming, so that Chinese students can directly understand his theory. This is a very good thing. (End)
